[SOURCE: Victoria CE Infant and Nursery School Phonics focus 05022025 (1).docx | Ofsted 26 Victoria  | Modified: 2025-05-09]

SEA Visit Report

School | Victoria Infant and Nursery School | Number | 912 | Date | 5th February 2025

Present: | Lisa Freeman, Head of School; Rebecca Roberts, Executive Headteacher; Linda Hardman, District School Effectiveness Lead for Dacorum; Feedback to governors. | Lisa Freeman, Head of School; Rebecca Roberts, Executive Headteacher; Linda Hardman, District School Effectiveness Lead for Dacorum; Feedback to governors. | Lisa Freeman, Head of School; Rebecca Roberts, Executive Headteacher; Linda Hardman, District School Effectiveness Lead for Dacorum; Feedback to governors. | Lisa Freeman, Head of School; Rebecca Roberts, Executive Headteacher; Linda Hardman, District School Effectiveness Lead for Dacorum; Feedback to governors. | Lisa Freeman, Head of School; Rebecca Roberts, Executive Headteacher; Linda Hardman, District School Effectiveness Lead for Dacorum; Feedback to governors.

Length of visit: Half a day plus preparation and report writing (Spring visit 1)

Purpose of visit and activities undertaken: To review the quality of early reading at the school.
This visit consisted of:
A discussion with the reading lead to discuss progress since the last inspection
A learning walk to see reading groups in Year 1
Information relating to Little Wandle Assessment tracker and impact
Hear year 1 and year 2 readers in the lowest 20% for each year group
Visits to phonics lessons in Nursery, Reception, Year 1 
A review of shared and published documentation relating to early reading

Context
When the school was last inspected in October 2023 there were some action points made relating to phonics and early reading:
“Reading has not been sufficiently prioritised. Teachers deliver the phonics scheme appropriately. However, there is not enough urgency when pupils fall behind. The weakest readers do not get effective support. The books pupils read are not precisely matched to the sounds they know. Consequently, they struggle to read fluently. While this is the case, the school has developed an effective culture of reading for pleasure. For example, the library has been improved considerably.”
“The school does not give the weakest readers the support they need. 
Pupils read books that do not match precisely enough the sounds they know. This means that pupils do not learn quickly to read with fluency. 
The school needs to review the support given to early readers, and ensure that this is provided effectively, so that the weakest readers remember their sounds better and can use these to build up their skills and confidence in reading.”
Outcomes for related to phonics

There were 44 pupils who were eligible for the phonics screening check in Year 1 in 2024; all of them sat the check and 4 pupils did not meet the phonics expected standard. I of these children is a disadvantaged learner
There were 10 pupils who were eligible for the phonics screening check in Year 2 in 2024; all of them sat the check and 7 pupils did not meet the phonics expected standard.  7 of these pupils were in receipt of SEN support, 3 children were disadvantaged learners and 1 pupil had English as an Additional Language (EAL).

Reading related outcomes in Early Years Foundation Stage (EYFS) in 2024


Main observations: 
Decisive, rapid and systematic action has been taken in response the Ofsted action points.  The success of these actions is clearly demonstrated in outcomes for early reading related outcomes in  2024.  Visits to the school confirm that there are some highly skilled practitioners who deliver the phonics and early reading programme in an effective manner.  
The school reviewed and changed its phonics teaching programme and now the school has Little Wandle Letters and Sounds revised embedded in practice.  The Assessment Tracker shared as part of this visit shows that pupil progress is meticulously tracked and tailored provision is promptly put in place for any child falling behind.
A further strength in provision is the school’s commitment to and engagement with the DFE funded English Hub Challenge.  This has ensured that the school:
Teaches with fidelity the chosen systematic synthetic phonics (SSP) programme 
Children make a strong start in reception
Teachers ensure a cumulative progression of sounds and books
Builds a team of expert reading teachers
Reaches those children falling behind the pace of the programme
Builds talking and listening activities into all activities across the school day
Develops pupils’ listening comprehension and language by reading aloud and talking bout stories, poems and non-fiction texts
Engagement with specialists with expertise in English has been impactful in enabling the school to further improve its provision in the areas of phonics, reading and writing.  A high level of commitment has been demonstrated by the school team and this is the reason for the success and rapid progress with this action point. 
The school has enacted the precise guidance given by the experts in this area.  Actions are identified in relation to the above elements for current areas of focus and the members of staff to whom these actions apply.  There is tight accountability and these actions are reviewed prior to the subsequent coaching session with the Literacy specialist who visits the school on a half termly basis.
In addition, the school uses the expertise of an HFL Teaching and Learning Adviser for English in a purposeful and effective manner.  The current focus for this work has been to provide the subject leader with writing assessment training and provide  support for the handwriting approach implementation.
The school leaders articulate, with clarity, the impact of the actions that have been taken to address the Ofsted action points relating to early reading.  The current phonics scheme has been well chosen, applied with fidelity and is impactful in terms of progression and outcomes.  Modelling strategies have grown capacity and there is an intentional commitment to ongoing and systematic training.  Assessment and monitoring strategies are being used in a purposeful manner to inform future planning for individual children.  
The choice of Little Wandle as the SSP programme was well planned.  If focuses purely on phonics and reading and the training is the highest priority. Staff are fully trained in the programme delivery before implementation.  The programme contains a thorough assessment and tracking stand which then enables forensic analysis and forward planning.  Care has been taken with the timetabling of the programme to ensure that decoding and fluency are fully embedded.  Children start the programme in Nursery, then it is followed through into Reception, Year 1 and Year 2.
Teachers are both confident and competent in their  delivery of the phonics programme.  The English Hub have validated this and these strengths were observed on this visit.  Action points are modelled and placed into staff meetings for consolidation.  Year 1 pupils are streamed in the afternoon to enable further consolidation in their learning of phonics.  The most effective practitioners support the  teaching of gaps.  Pace of the teaching sequence is observed to have become more rapid and effective. 
The school has a comprehensive summary of the intent, implementation and impact of the reading curriculum at the school.  It is aligned to the requirements of the inspection framework.  It is a helpful summary because it summarises how the intent, implementation and impact is underpinned at the school.  There is clarity about the pedagogy, how children with SEND are supported, the role of the subject leader and the formative and summative assessment strategies.  In addition the implementation is clarified through the school’s approach to teaching fluency, vocabulary and comprehension.  There is further detail related to recommended reading lists which are well represented on the school website, whole school reading related events, daily story time and 1:1 reading opportunities.  The culture of reading is well developed at the school and this is outlined in expectations regarding reading at home, reading areas in school, the school library and the support provided by reading volunteers.  Reading for pleasure was clearly indicated as a strength at the last inspection and its success has continued to grow.  The school assesses the impact in terms of pupil voice, evidence in knowledge and skills and the outcomes children achieve, which in 2024 were above national standards and the higher local standards for Hertfordshire.  
Banded books used by the school are  a mixture of  “Big Cat” and others.  The school uses the Little Wandle books which are matched to the correct phonic phase.  Books that were not decodable have been discarded.  All reading books were completely matched to phonic sounds.  A grant of £6000 from English Hub was provided to pay for the phonic scheme, resources, books and supply costs for training.  Pupil progress is tracked by the phonic phase books.  This then generates questions through pupil progress meetings to inform adjustments to planning for individual children going forward.
The school website is both informative and supportive.  The curriculum is well represented.  There is detailed guidance for parents relating to the phonics programme and reading.  This includes documents such as the reading progression plan and recommended reads for each year group. 
Strong evidence was shared in relation to parental partnership.  There is comprehensive and supportive information for parents on the school website related to phonics and through the school’s approach to engaging parents in the learning process for their child.  A phonic workshop takes place in the autumn term primarily for the Reception and Year 1 parents.  Teachers communicate the sounds the children are working through fortnightly newsletters in Reception.  The nursery newsletters concentrate on rhymes and environmental sounds and the exploration of specific sounds.  Year 1 provide this information through the homework books.  “Reading with your child” is modelled to the parents.  Parental consultation sessions provide information about gaps and reading development skills.  The school is proactive with parents regarding any reading concerns and signposts additional support.

Little Wandle Assessment Tracker 
This is working well and is carefully monitored. Leaders have been able to maximise its use due to the guidance received from the English Hub.  Overviews from Little Wandle keeps teachers and leaders on track.  This is also moderated  by teacher assessment for each child.  Heat maps are created and can identify the bottom 20% of readers.  Patterns are identified in terms of who knows the different sounds.  Reteaching then takes place where appropriate.  The tracker enables the staff to identify children needing overlearning and consolidation.  Summary analysis can be competed for different purposes and enhances the subject leader’s knowledge of individual and class performance.  Leaders insist that there is complete fidelity to the scheme.  It them becomes predictable and systematic and progresses the learning rapidly for individual learners.  This is then the springboard for success with wider learning opportunities across the curriculum.
Hearing readers in the bottom 20%
Children in Year 1 and Year 2 at the early stages of fluency were observed reading to a familiar adult.  Children were reading books that matched their phonic phase of development.  Reading behaviours are developmental and the children were at different stages of acquiring phonics and fluency confidence.  The prognosis for all children is positive and it is clear to see the impact of the phonics programme on their progress.  The Year 2 children are likely to achieve success in the phonic screening test when they retake it.  Adults have been well trained to support readers acquire decoding and fluency skills.  Book talk skills were demonstrated at appropriate times to support recall, comprehension and prediction.  Children were encouraged to sound out and blend in their heads.  They could segment words and put them together.  Modelling of “my turn, your turn” was used at timely points.  Pronunciation was corrected when needed.  The more fluent the children were in their reading,  the more they were able to use the skills of prediction to help them make sense of the story.  They were also able to self-correct and increasingly able to use punctuation to support reading with expression.
Visits to the phonics sessions
Provision observed in the phonics sessions was strong and effective and there was rapid progress in learning during the snapshots observed.  This is because the school has some highly skilled expert teachers of phonics.  In Nursery children begin the Foundation programme for Little Wandle.  Songs and rhymes through video are used.  During this lesson children were identifying how many syllables there were in each word.  Actions were used to embed the learning where possible. Repetition was well used to reinforce and consolidate the learning.  Modelling was of high quality and children demonstrated confidence practising their sounds and accuracy in identifying sounds.  A blending activity took place using some magnetic letters and children demonstrated accuracy and competence in their sounding out of the sounds and words. The teaching sequence of revisit teach practice and apply the phonic sounds was explicit and children were highly engaged because the quality of teaching was of an exemplary standard and covered at a slick pace.  
High quality phonics teaching was similarly observed in reception led by skilled practitioners.  Pupils recapped prior leaning and practised blending words together.  Individual support was targeted enabling engagement.  Corrections were made appropriately and teaching assistant support was being used effectively to support the learning development.  Progression was clear as children were demonstrating success with chunking and blending longer words.  Children were able to rehearse and practice with their learning partners.  Some excellent modelling was observed which made the sounds explicit for the children.  There was clear confidence in the delivery and this is because teachers have such a strong level of subject knowledge.  Behaviour management was observed to be skilled and this enabled pace and progress to be rapid.
In the Year 1 class children were recapping their speedy sounds to test their recall of prior learning.  They were able to blend words accurately.  Tricky words were recapped and the new sound was introduced.  Clear connections between the grapheme and the phonemes were understood by the children.  The direct teaching was effective and progressed the learning.  There was not clarity in this part of the lesson relating to the role of the teaching assistant so this is worth revisiting to ensure consistency of approach across the school.

Visits to reading groups
Children in Year 2 were exploring the text “The Boastful Turtle”  and there was an inference focus to this lesson – a higher order reading skill.  The visualiser was used well to enable text analysis and children were being prompted to uplevel vocabulary.  There was careful targeting and support provided to children with individual needs and it was clear to see the skilful practical application of VIPERS (vocabulary, infer, predict, explain, retrieve, sequence, summarise) – the reading domains which support the development of pupils’ comprehension skills.
In Year 1 the impact of the work that has been completed with The English Hub can be clearly evidenced.  The reading sessions focus on decoding, prosody – reading with meaning stress and intonation and comprehension – and understanding the text. Energy could be observed in the reading groups.  Pupil groupings are targeted to support individual needs.  Correct sounds were modelled and questioning strategies were observed to be intuitive and effective.  There is a programme withing Little Wandle that progresses the learning of children with SEND.  Children are taught GPC (grapheme phoneme correspondence) in words sentences and decodable books.  (Graphemes are letters and letter combinations, phonemes are the speech sounds).  This was observed being delivered in a skilled and progressive manner in the Year 1 classroom.  We could see a consistent approach being used in the reading groups.  The correct terminology is being used by the staff.  Children demonstrate increasing confidence in blending strategies and children with more complex special needs are also enabled to access the programme to progress their reading skills. 

In summary
Exemplary progress is observed to have been made in response to this OFSTED key point for action.  The leaders and staff term deserve recognition for their commitment and determination to demonstrate high quality standards in this critical area of learning.  This visit demonstrated:
Reading has been the highest priority.  Embracing the guidance from The English Hub has made the difference.
There is an urgent, responsive approach if pupils start to fall behind in their phonic acquisition.  This is supported through the capacity, skilled and timely use of the Little Wandle tracking system. 
The weakest readers get effective support. This has been observed through the skilled delivery of the  SEND programme with staff who have been trained comprehensively to deliver this to a high standard.
Pupils read books that match the sounds they know. This means that pupils are learning to  read quickly with fluency.

Recommendations: 
Consider what reading related activities might be best for children to complete independently as part of the reading session when the adults are working with guided groups of children
Further develop the role of the teaching assistants in relation to supporting learning development to ensure consistency of approach across all classrooms.  You have strong practitioners for are valuable assets to the school.  Aim for consistency in approach for the maximum impact on learning.
Continue to develop parental engagement in the learning process for phonics and early reading.  You have many families who will want to engage and support their child’s learning and this is a further asset for the school.

Date and purpose of next visit: 19th March 2025
                                                         Focus to be confirmed

Name: | Linda A Hardman | School Effectiveness Adviser

[SOURCE: HFL School Review Action Plan-reviewed April 2024.docx | Ofsted 26 Victoria  | Modified: 2025-04-14]

Area of improvement | Actions | Timeframe | Staff involved | Impact

Phonics/reading | Fully adopt Little Wandle (LW) for phonics programme in Year 1. | To start after half term break | New members of staff and ECT | 68% YR1 children passed mock PSC March 24
75% YR1 children passed mock PSC April 24

75% YR1 are on track with phonics (LW Spring 2 Assessment)

75% of Reception on track with all aspects of LW
88% of Year 1 on track with all aspects of LW
(Summer 1 assessment)

91% YR1 children passed PSC
30% YR2 children passed PSC retake

See Heatmaps for Reception and Year 1 assessments.

Phonics/reading | Fully adopt LW for phonics programme in reception.
To concentrate on reading and not writing during phonics sessions for the short term, until LW has been adopted. | To start in the summer term.
To start asap. | Reception team | All children have started reading groups at start of summer 1. After each assessment point reading groups reviewed using LW tracker, all children either move up or remain at their current level.
Writing is part of the enhancements and modelled outside of phonics- 74% Reception are on track with writing- continued focus for summer term.
English Hub Action plans have been shared and put in place after Spring 1 and 2 visits- stating in Spring 2
“The school has made good progress in implementing the points since the last visit.” Teachers us the correct resources and weekly lesson plans to follow the structure”, Teachers use the correct language to encourage pupils to decode and then blend words.

Phonics/reading | Catch up sessions for pupils in Year 2 to use LW. | Asap but at least for after half term | AHT (Sarah) | Pupils in Year 2 not meeting reading expectations have been grouped in Phase 2, 3 and 5 phonics and reading groups to reduce the gap.
Teachers running groups for most catch up sessions.

Phonics/reading | New LW reading books to be circulated. | Asap but at least for after half term | HoS | Completed- no other books sent home and parents informed in writing and invited to a LW presentation. All reading books are matched to the child’s ability to read fluently.
English Hub Report Spring 1 and 2- “Staff use LW reading books to ensure reading books are closely matched to their ability to read tricky words and blending ability.”

Phonics/reading | Visit to Thomas Coram to discuss the reading curriculum with reading leader (Rebecca Monro) | Before half term. | AHT (Sarah) | Reading lessons changed to ensure consistency with Victoria and TC and using Reading Shed texts/lesson plans.
Lessons more targeted and reading skills explored following the updated Reading Framework- “comprehension is an outcome of reading lots, broadening vocabulary and developing knowledge. It is not something that can be taught in its own right. The reading approach in Year 2 develops children’s love of reading, automaticity and fluency, and consequently comprehension”

Phonics/reading | Clarify the reading curriculum. Year 1 teachers to implement. | To start after half term | Year 1 team | Children read twice a week -first session decode and second prosody/comprehension. Parent voice has been significant improvement in confidence of their children reading with fluency.
Once a week whole class reading lesson in Year 1 to focus on an extract to mirror Year 2.

Phonics/reading | Reading training to be in place for Year 2 team with Vicky Pearson at Thomas Coram. | During the next half term. | Year 2 team | Completed in Spring 2 and discussed reading curriculum, reading lessons and how to introduce whole class reading lessons to Year 1- from this discussion Year 1 in Summer 1 have started to use VIPER lessons (as modelled in Year 2) as an addition to the LW reading groups.

Phonics/reading | To revert to VIPERS and Reading Shed in Year 2 for the interim. | Asap but at least for after half term. | Year 2 team | Completed

Phonics/reading | New reading curriculum to be implemented. | To start in summer term | Year 2 team | LF drafted reading curriculum which has been shared with SLT and SEA to be rolled out ASAP.

EYFS | To complete a review of the EYFS curriculum. Discuss with EYA on how she can support leaders. | 07.02.24 | EYFS leader | EYA looked at curriculum and SL are working with EYFS lead to ensure clear links are in place from EYFS to Year 2. History SL designing new history curriculum with HFL advisor in summer term.

EYFS | EYFS curriculum to be updated and implemented. | To start in summer term | EYFS leader | See above.
Had EYFS EYA monitoring visit to focus on assessment and pupil intervention to highlight specific targets/interventions for children who were boarder line GLD.

EYFS | SEA to liaise with EYA for future monitoring/actions to support leaders | On-going | EYFS leader | Focus on enhancements to develop learning and moderated current assessment data March 24 to ensure focused interventions are put in place to maximise the number of children reaching GLD.

Staffing | Interim review of performance management objectives to hold staff to account. To include QoE and inclusion. Updated following any monitoring. | To start before half term | HoS and EHT | All staff have had mid reviews- see SEND ASV report focusing on the outcome below,
Outcome 2a: exploring teachers’ understanding of the needs of children with SEND and how teachers differentiate and use distinctive teaching approaches to engage and support them- graded as expected.
Action plans have been put in place after mid-point reviews. These have been conducted with HR and regular reviews booked to check progress on action plans every 2 to 4 weeks.

Staffing | HR discussion for actions to address staff long term absence. Possible support from occupational health and HR with attendance improvement plans. | asap | HoS and EHT | Completed- no staff member had met threshold for attendance improvement plans. Ali Stevens from HFL HR has reviewed.
Return to work meetings are completed and logged to highlight with staff the importance of good attendance, support that can be offered etc.

Staffing | Review for possible recruitment for inclusion leader. | By the end of spring term | HoS and EHT | Increased SENCO from 1 day to 1.5 days continuing from Sept to enable additional CPD for staff and monitoring of SEND children and impact of interventions/ISPs.

Mathematics | To continue implementing the Essentialmaths curriculum. | Now | R-Y 2 teachers | Completed and SLA supporting VG to ensure consistently taught across the school. Reviewed EYFS to ensure coverage completed before Year 1.
Modelled maths lesson for ECT and worked together to improve LO and activities in maths using Essentials.

Mathematics | Address QFT concerns through additional monitoring and performance management objectives. Focus on the progress of the lower 20% of pupils during visits to lessons.  Adaptative teaching, pace and engaging teaching should be monitored closely. Sharing what good effective teaching looks like throughout the team. To begin monitoring the highlighted classes. Current status is good or better teaching at 50%. | On-going but should start asap. | HoS, EHT and AHT. | Staff Meeting- on collaborative planning, coverage across all year groups, book look and setup expectations for work and refresh of using the practise sheets from Essentials with the steps to follow.
Planning using Essentials with HFL booked 22 May with Year 1 ECT and maths lead.

Mathematics | Finalise any adaptations to the curriculum (after mastery training) for September. Track and match EYFS and KS1 curriculum. Focus on vocabulary to begin with. | On-going but should start asap. | Maths leader | Maths lead focusing on where adaptations should be in own class- focus is on using Essentials and mastery approaches to give more depth to the activities. 
Focus has been on Stem sentences and speaking in full mathematical sentences and smaller steps using Essentials planning.

History and geography curriculum | Liaise with humanities staff at Thomas Coram and/or Chorley Wood. | Before the end of the spring term | Humanities leaders | Completed.
See visit report from Claire Watson- completed curriculum plan for History and will be working with Geography leads in summer term to mirror the same work.

History and geography curriculum | Seek further advice to review the precision of the agreed curriculums.   Kate.Kellner-Dilks@hfleducation.org | Before the end of the spring term | Humanities leaders | Completed- working with History leads from both schools to review the History curriculum.
Victoria teachers had CDP with HFL on assessment in Foundation Subjects Spring term highlighting a range of AFL activities.
All SL had training on Securing your Subject with Rebecca Collins Summer 1.

[SOURCE: Admission Minutes 2025-06-16.doc | Ofsted 26 Victoria /Minutes/Admissions/2025-26 | Modified: 2026-02-01]




Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

 Minutes of the Meeting of the Admissions Committee held on 
Monday 16th June 2025
Online
Present:	
Mrs E Bunn (EB)
Mrs L Freeman
Miss L Hill

Mrs B Roberts (BR, Executive Head)
Fr S Owen (SO)

Also in attendance:
Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional          


Apologies:  Mr N Goss (NG, Chair)

1
Welcome and confidentiality reminder
EB opened the meeting and reminded the committee about confidentiality.


2
Conflicts of Interests and apologies for absence.
No conflict of interest, apologies of absence received and accepted from 
Mr N Goss


3Minutes of the meeting held on 13th January 2025
The minutes of the meeting were agreed and would be signed using the GH.

Matters arising

Action points

CW to send NG instructions on how to complete the signature facility on Governor Hub, by 14th January 2025 - completed
All admission documents to be uploaded to the next FGB meeting folder on Governor Hub by 15th January 2025 - completed
NG to investigate the option of using his PDF checker to assess accessibility of the admission policies, in addition to wider use on the new website, and feedback to BR by 31st January 2025 - completed
BR to ensure the admission policies are submitted to HCC for Thomas Coram and Victoria, by 7th March 2025 - completed
BR to ensure the admission policy and associated documents for Thomas Coram and Victoria are on the HCC and school website by 15th March 2025 - completed





4
Do governors wish to consult in the next round of admissions?

It was agreed that governors do not wish to consult on admissions this year.

 
 

5
In Year admissions – decision on whether to continue with the Federation processing In-Year admissions or using Herts County Council (HCC)?

Currently the Federation manages the In-Year admissions process and BR advised that she felt this was the most effective system rather than using HCC.

Q – Are there any benefits to using HCC?
A – BR confirmed that using HCC offers no advantages; however, continuing with the current process provides benefits, including greater efficiency and faster admission of children

EB requested that CW upload the admission policies to the ‘Policies’ folder on Governor Hub.

It was agreed that the Federation would continue using their in-year admissions process.















CW
6
Consideration of pupil repeating a year – see document on Governor Hub

Governors confirmed that they had reviewed the letter from the parents and had considered the information provided.

BR confirmed that the Admissions Policy states that children should be educated in the correct chronological year group, with the curriculum differentiated accordingly, to meet their needs. This is in line with HCC’s policy and DfE guidance, which states that children should be educated in their normal age group.

LF advised governors that the parents had not made a formal request to the previous school for the child to repeat Nursery, however they had discussed the matter and agreed that the child would not repeat Nursery. The child does not have any physical difficulties and does not have any external agencies supporting him. He was seen by an Occupational Therapist (OT) however this report has not been shared by the parents. 

He does not have any formal diagnosis, and parents have discussed that they do not wish to pursue any further investigations into receiving a formal diagnosis and were satisfied with the Individual Learning Plan that has been developed by Victoria school.

BR informed governors that the class teacher and LF were confident that the child was accessing the curriculum effectively, however parents raised a concern about his social and emotional development, due to his experience at his previous school.

Q – What is the plan going forward, would he always remain out of his normal year group?
A – When he leaves Victoria, he could move straight to Year 4, not all schools would accommodate a child out of their normal year group. This has been explained to parents; however they are not concerned about this aspect of his future education and instead are more concerned with his current situation, they feel he is not ready for the transition into Year 1.

Q – How is the child progressing?
A - He is meeting 75% of the early learning objectives and has picked up reading very well, despite initially struggling to engage.

Q – How does that compare with his peers?
A – There are other children within the cohort that are not progressing as well as him. He is slightly below the national average, which is approximately 80%. 

BR informed governors that, unless there is compelling evidence from the class teacher, identifying additional special educational needs and specialist reports, recommending the child remain in Reception for a second year, the Federation would not recommend approving the request. LF added that, in summer 2024, there were children performing below his current level who have since transitioned to Year 1 and thrived. She also expressed concern that remaining in Reception and working alongside younger children could be more detrimental to his wellbeing.

Q – What has been communicated to parents? In their letter they refer to concerns being raised by the teacher.
A – His class teacher had mentioned that he is working slightly below the national average, at 75%, however she does not feel this warrants him remaining in Reception year for a second year. 

Q – The parents refer to a conversation regarding holding him back a year, when he first joined the school, could you elaborate.
A – During their initial tour of the school, prior to their child joining, the parents raised concerns and considered the option of him remaining in Nursery for an additional year. However, they decided to have the child join Reception as this was the most suitable course of action.

LF explained to the parents that any decision regarding a child repeating a year lies with the school and the governing body. She also emphasised that, without having worked with the child, it would be difficult to make an informed judgement at that stage. LF has since apologised for any initial confusion and confirmed that the child has settled in well, with no concerns raised by the class teacher or other staff that would support a recommendation for him to repeat a year.

Q – The parent implied that they believed an informal agreement had been reached, following your conversation. Did they follow up on this?  Did they submit a formal written request
A – The class teacher met with the parent to create an Individual Learning Plan for him, there was no formal request made to repeat Reception, parents were happy with the adjustments and interventions provided. 

LF informed governors that she had explained to the parents that they had the option to apply for Higher Needs Funding. However, the parents chose not to pursue this and reiterated their decision not to seek a formal diagnosis for their son, as they did not want him to feel different from other children.

Q – When is his birthday and are there other children comparable to him?
A – His birthday falls in June, and there are around 10 summer-born children in the cohort. While some summer-born pupils may require additional support, this is not the case for all. Children often develop significantly during Year 1, and by Year 2, they tend to progress at varying rates

Q – The parents referenced the DfE guidance, but I could not find any recommendation suggesting that repeating Reception would be beneficial. In fact, the guidance indicates that doing so could have a negative impact on the child, what do you think?
A – The DfE evidence relates to children starting Reception. The parents have expressed regret about not having their child repeat Nursery. However, LF and BR agree with the governors that the DfE does not strongly advocate for the repetition of Reception

EB explained that the parent believes moving to Year 1 would have a negative impact on their child’s social and emotional wellbeing. However, the DfE guidance EB reviewed does not support this view and, in fact, suggests the opposite. BR agreed that this is the opinion of the teachers working with the child. LF added that there are no external agencies involved, no EHCP in place, and the child has been thriving. She confirmed that he will continue to receive the same support and will have a smooth and well-supported transition

Q – Have you received any reports for external agencies such as the OT?
A – We understand from parents that there are currently no external agencies involved with the child and that the OT was completed in the previous school. Parents have offered to supply OT report and evidence from “educational professionals” but this evidence was not included with their letter to governors.

Q – What is the deadline to respond to parents?
A – We would like to respond as soon as possible as the transition period starts next week.

Q – I notice there is no right to appeal and this committee is classed as the admissions authority. I feel that we should review all the available evidence, prior to making our final decision. Could we ask for the OT report despite parents not being forthcoming with providing it?
A – BR agreed that reviewing the full report would reflect the governors’ due diligence and advised that it is important for making an informed decision. Given the tight timeframe, parents should be asked to submit the report by the end of the day tomorrow.

Governors requested that LF should ask parents for the report from the OT and any other external agencies. Governors and Senior Leaders will reconvene before the end of the week to consider all further evidence and reach a decision.



7
Meeting dates 2025

2nd July       FGB Procedural         TC


8
Any other business

No further business was raised.


8Has the meeting been conducted in line with our vision and values? Has the board focused on all pupils and staff being able to flourish in learning and love? Has the meeting been conducted with kindness, respect, resilience and thankfulness?

It was agreed that the meeting had been conducted in line with our vision and values.


9
Action points
CW to upload the admission policies to the ‘Policies’ folder on Governor Hub by 27th June 2025.
LF to request OT reports and any additional reports from parents by the morning of 17th June 2025.


9
Close of Meeting
There being no further business the meeting closed at 2.15pm.











Flourishing in learning and love. 'Do everything in love.' (1 Corinthians 16:14)
	
Minutes of Castle Federation Admissions: 16th June 2025

[SOURCE: P&C Minutes 2025-12-10.docx | Ofsted 26 Victoria /Minutes/P&C/2025-26 | Modified: 2025-12-18]

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

Minutes of the Pupil and Curriculum Meeting held on 

Wednesday 10th December 2025 - Online

Chaired by Mrs N Boddam-Whetham

  Present:

There being no further business the meeting closed at 8.45pm. 

Ms R Roberts (BR, Exec Head)
Mrs L Hill (LH, Head of Thomas Coram)
Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria)
Mrs E Bunn (EB, Chair)
Mrs K Hennessey (KH) | Mr I Davies (ID)
Mrs T Brown (TB)
Fr S Owen (SO)
Mrs N Boddam-Whetham (NB-W)
Mrs L Preston (LPr)

Apologies received: Stacy Giles (SG)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional, Lisa Forde (LFo) and 
Tim Trailor (TT) | Apologies received: Stacy Giles (SG)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional, Lisa Forde (LFo) and 
Tim Trailor (TT)

1 | Welcome, Opening Prayers and Confidentiality Reminder
KH opened the meeting at 7pm and confirmed that this would be her last meeting and NB-W will be taking over as Chair. SO led the committee in prayer. 

Governors welcomed LPr to the P&C committee.

Colleagues were reminded of the confidentiality of the meeting. 

AOB – Appreciation for KH’s hard work and commitment

2 | Conflicts of Interest and Apologies for Absence
Apologies were received and accepted from SG.

No conflicts of interest declared.

3 | Minutes of P&C meeting 4th June 2025 and Matters Arising
The Governing Board approved the previous minutes, these will be marked as agreed on Governor Hub.

Matters arising from meeting of 4th June 2025:
CW to amend the terms of reference accordingly and upload to Governor Hub, by 15th June - completed
BR will propose a revised timetable to EB for 2025-26, by 15th June - completed
CW to update the SEND policy with NB-W as link governor, by 16th June - completed
Suspension and Permanent Exclusion Policy – CW to make the required grammar amendment by 15th June - completed

4 | Current pupils’ data -  Lisa Forde (LFo)
LFo advised governors that her presentation focused on reviewing the current Year 5 data, specifically looking at where the current Year 6 pupils were when they were in Year 5, in order to evaluate the impact of Pixl. The analysis highlighted some areas for improvement where additional support should be focused; however, overall, the impact has been very successful.

LFo clarified that pupils were assessed in weeks 4 and 5 of the autumn term, providing a baseline.
Blue indicates pupils are working at nearly greater depth or greater depth
Green indicates expected, nearly there, and those expected to achieve by the end of the year. 
‘B’ indicates pupils who are unlikely to meet the expected standard unless significant additional provision is put in place to support them.

LFo highlighted the following points:
Year 6 levels were low; therefore an additional teacher has been allocated to Year 6 to support them.
Reading has been significantly improved, with 40% of children at greater depth and 77% at expected, which is an excellent achievement at this time of the year.
Writing continues to be a concern across the school
The federation has subscribed to White Rose learning, which follows a concrete pictorial abstract approach allowing children to draw the problem, supporting problem-solving and reasoning, and provides additional challenge for more able learners.
Pupil progress meetings took place in October, during which teachers demonstrated a strong understanding of their pupils and their learning gaps, supported by the effective use of Pixl.

Q - Why is there discrepancy across the subjects?
A - Some teachers may be stronger at teaching reading, for example, however as a federation we are striving for high academic achievement, with an increased focus on supporting teachers. There is an improving picture in maths, but there is further work required. 

Q - How does the current Year 6 data compare with last year’s figures?
A – There is no significant difference

Q - What impact has the introduction of the new scheme had on teachers, and how confident are you that it will support improvement moving forward?
A – The White Rose scheme provides a high level of support for teachers, including videos, lesson plans and has been very well received by teachers.

Q: What could prevent you from achieving this improvement?
A: Teachers can sometimes feel constrained by the curriculum, so it is important to allow time for flexibility. We encourage teachers to be creative and to inspire pupils.


Governors agreed that the data was insightful, highlighting key gaps, and supported the implementation of a new scheme.

5 | Curriculum update 
SEND Ordinary Provision

TC
LD highlighted the key focus areas:
White Rose introduced for Maths
Herts Essentials
Teachers have been coached through joint teaching and peer observation, which has been a valuable exercise, enabling them to take ideas back to their classrooms and implement them.
Learning walks have been conducted across the school and general feedback has been provided to the whole school, supporting staff CPD.

Q: Will the learning walk observations be included in appraisals?
A: Observations provide useful feedback, though no formal feedback was planned. Any issues were addressed with teachers, and as targets were set in September aligned to the School Improvement Plan, the observations may not directly affect them.

Victoria
LF highlighted the following key areas of focus:
Focus on building strong foundations in reading, writing, and maths.
Essentials Writing has been embedded in Years 1 and 2 and is now being rolled out in Early Years. The Early Years adviser praised the exceptional mark-making and suggested sharing it with other settings.
Significant contribution from an ECT, with “tool of the week” initiatives (e.g., gel pens, highlighters) creating excitement and engagement.
Emphasis on handwriting and number recognition. Book looks to identify issues and following a review with LF, teachers have implemented creative approaches focusing on quality over quantity to improve outcomes.
History curriculum will move to Kapow after Christmas.
LF and BR reviewed books of vulnerable children, gaining valuable insights. LF is compiling a list of key concepts for specific staff to check a pupils’ understanding.

SEND Ordinary Provision
BR confirmed that the Herts SEN team produced a comprehensive document. It includes a definition of Ordinary Provision, which the school is meeting with no concerns; it also provides helpful links to the toolkit.

Governors asked whether a succession plan is in place for the SENDCo. BR explained that a teacher is currently undertaking the SENDCo qualification as part of her CPD; should a vacancy arise, she would then be able to apply for the role.

6 | SEA visit report
The visit was cancelled by the SEA at Victoria and the report from the visit to Thomas Coram has not yet been received.

7 | Update on reading, phonics knowledge and language comprehension  

LF advised governors:
Graduated phonics and Little Wandle continue to be implemented, with two further monitoring visits planned. 
Phonics and reading groups are tracked regularly, and additional in-class phonics interventions are in place where needed.
All but one child in Reception are reading banded books. 
In Year 1, 75% of pupils are currently at the expected level for reading.

Governors acknowledged the strong progress being made. When asked about higher-attaining pupils, it was reported that approximately eight pupils in Year 2 are currently working at greater depth. These pupils transitioned directly from Little Wandle in Year 1 to banded books. By the end of the previous academic year, 40% of pupils were assessed as working at greater depth.

8 | Pupil Premium strategy for website - update

BR advised governors that VIP training has been undertaken with HfL, with significant work focused on refining the language used in the statement, across the federation. Lucy, Lisa and BR are currently fine-tuning the Pupil Premium strategy with a strong emphasis on supporting all of the  the most vulnerable pupils. The schools are two of 21 participating in the VIP pilot, which includes weekly meetings with individual pupils and a clearer academic focus.

Q: Do the children wear a badge to identify them as VIPs?
A: The children at TC requested badges; while these are not currently available at Victoria, due to the age of the child, pupils wear their VIP badges with pride at TC.

9 | Outcome of monitoring activities – classroom visits

Governors agreed that this point had been covered earlier in the discussion.

10 | Link visit reports
ID confirmed that he has observed all the areas discussed by LF in the above minutes. He also noted that the planned English visit will be rescheduled due to recent staffing changes.

SH and LPr carried out a joint Maths visit as part of the handover process; however, the notes are currently in draft form and will be shared once the teacher has had the opportunity to review them.

NB-W gave an in-depth report at the FGB, where she stated that she was impressed with the level of Church Distinctiveness being carried out.

11 | Pupil Council/ Eco/Spiritual ambassadors  Leaders advised governors that:
The Pupil Parliament raised £106 through the sale of pre-loved Christmas jumpers.
The Spiritual Ambassadors have been working closely with Father Stuart and lead a collective worship each term, for example Harvest in the autumn term and the Parable of the Prodigal Son in the spring term.
As part of Kindness at Victoria, a Year 2 pupil submitted a successful bid for £150, which generated great excitement. This funding has supported the creation of a kindness stop in the playground and the purchase of high-visibility jackets for Kindness Ambassadors, linked to the 52 Lives initiative. Pupils also visited the food bank, which was a highly engaging experience.

12 | Pupil Surveys
BR advised that the overall feedback was very positive, with 100% of pupils stating that they are kind to others.

One concern raised by governors was that 15% of pupils in Year 1 reported that they do not feel safe. LF advised that they felt this may relate to their understanding of the question or the language used and is something she will be following up.

Governors queried why 21% of children stated that they cannot attend a range of clubs, either because they are unable to access one or feel that suitable options are not available. LD advised that a recurring theme was interest in construction-based activities, such as a Lego club, which is being considered. It was also noted that a significant number of pupils with SEN currently attend clubs.

13 | Policies/Guidance for review include (on Gov Hub):

Governors approved the following policies:
Behaviour Policy
RE Policy
Supporting Children with Medical Conditions
Governors queried how supply teachers are made aware of an IHCP, BR confirmed this forms part of a handover with a staff member, adding that the office manage the short or long term medication, maintaining consistency. All plans are on medical tracker. EB stated that there are some variations in font colour that should be updated by CW prior to being uploaded to the website.
British Values Statement for Victoria
British Values Statement for Thomas Coram | CW

12 | Executive Headteacher’s Report (including FIP RAG rating and three-year oracy plan)

BR provided an overview for Governors:
Oracy objectives on the FIP are being slightly amended. An interim three-year oracy plan is in place, with the intention of adopting the full oracy programme next year.
Inclusion of the most vulnerable children remains a significant focus for the Federation. Work has progressed quickly to embed this approach across both schools, developing the philosophy behind it, strengthening relationships, and ensuring vulnerable pupils feel a sense of belonging—identified as fundamental. This work was deemed essential even before its increased prominence in the Ofsted framework.

Q: What are the implications of the changes to TA and LSA roles in terms of pay banding, staff views, and budget impact?
A: No concerns have been raised and the increased cost was included in the budget. It was considered morally right to ensure equality of pay and consistent treatment across all staff. Governors agreed that this was very important.

Q: Regarding maternity cover and successful candidates appointed—Is there scope to retain these staff? Were they recruited through an agency?
A: Retention can be considered if suitable vacancies arise, and this presents a positive opportunity to secure high-quality staff. One candidate was recruited through an agency.

Q: The Every Child Programme includes 71 pupils (VIPs), which seems high—are only TAs involved?
A: LD confirmed that considerable time was taken to allocate pupils to staff. Twenty-seven staff members volunteered, including office staff, TAs, and teachers. Meetings take place during break times, lunchtimes, and soft starts. The programme is working well, and LD proposed that a staff voice would be conducted to obtain further feedback on the success. Staff have specific focus areas to cover with their allocated pupils.
Governors noted that this is a very rewarding role and agreed that the programme provides strong support for VIP pupils.


Heads of school’s report

Thomas Coram
LD advised that the format of the report was changed in line with Ofsted criteria. Governors agreed it was a very clear and concise report and found the new format very easy to access. 

LD has introduced peer coaching with a structured plan over the year to include peer observations. LD informed governors that this has led to extensive learning walks where significant improvements in the teaching and learning have been evidenced.

LD clarified that the Year 3–6 baseline assessment data indicated low writing outcomes; however, this reflects the fact that some content has not yet been taught. It is therefore expected that writing achievement will be higher by the end of the year.

LD informed governors that a recent pupil survey showed that 100% of respondents reported feeling proud to be part of Team TC, which Governors agreed was a very positive outcome. 


Victoria Head’s report

LF informed governors that a key priority is embedding an inclusion thread across the curriculum and carrying out significant work with VIPs. Considerable work is also taking place on developing core skills, particularly early reading and writing. LF and BR have spent substantial time evaluating progress across the school.

Governors agreed to focus on how their link subject is celebrated and validated during their visits to aid their review.

IDSR – (on Gov Hub - you need to download to access the weblink)

This provides an overview of the school including areas such as the profile and outcomes, which provides governors with a vital analysis of the school. The Federation SEA will support governors using this tool during a training session in January, where the focus will be reviewing Victoria’s IDSR. Any specific questions governors would like to address in the training session should be emailed to LF and BR by 7th January.

Governors queried the following acronyms:

CIN – Child in Need
FSM6 – Free School Meal Ever 6
EAL – English Additional Language
ACE – Adverse Childhood Experience – BR added that across the federation, VIPs are graded according to the number of Adverse Childhood Experiences (ACEs) they have encountered, such as family separation, parental substance misuse, or exposure to domestic violence

TC’s SIAMS self-evaluation document 
LD informed governors that Lisa from the Diocese conducted a SIAMS review in the summer. Following her feedback, the school’s approach has been updated, and this work is continuing.
.

13 | Pupil numbers in Berkhamsted 
Victoria meeting with planning team 
Planning team discussion at local HT’s meeting

BR informed governors that Hertfordshire, and Berkhamsted in particular, have been affected by a falling birth rate, resulting in increased competition between schools for pupil places. Significant work has taken place at Victoria, including enhanced school tours, and numbers have improved, with 30 pupils now in Nursery compared to 17 last year. This, governors agreed reflects a strong approach,
.
LF was contacted by the planning team regarding a review of pupil numbers, which BR also attended. The planning team is assessing projections and considering whether Victoria and another local school may need to move from two-form to one-form entry. This would also impact Thomas Coram, with a possible change to two form entry. BR has spoken with the Diocesan Admissions Officer, Maggie, and SEA, providing a rationale for why a reduction in PAN is not currently necessary. Any change to PAN would require an 18-month consultation.

The planning team attended the BASH meeting and reiterated that all schools in Berkhamsted need to consider solutions. If no school volunteers to reduce its PAN, the council may be required to impose changes.

The planning team have since apologised for their initial approach and confirmed that they will continue discussions with all Berkhamsted schools. LF, LD, TT, EB and BR will meet the planning team and report back to governors.

Governors thanked BR for her hard work on this matter.

14 | GDPR update 
BR reminded governors that the federation has moved to HFL for GDPR and DPO support. TR has met with the DPO, and several updates to documentation are required. CW was thanked for supporting TR with these updates.
.

15 | Website compliance
LF and LD have been carefully reviewing the website to ensure all information is up to date. Only minor adjustments were needed.
Governors agreed that this reflects the school’s effectiveness in maintaining compliance.

16 | Investment update
TT reported that £41,000 is held by the Diocese, for TC with a further £12,500 transferred to the Diocese recently. BR and TT met with the investment advisers, who recommended placing the funds in low-risk bonds, in line with the current investment of the £41,000 held by the Diocese in the school’s name. Governors agreed with the investment recommendation.

TT also informed governors that a further £2,500 is held in the names of the two priests personally. TT has passed the necessary paperwork to them, and they will need to liaise with the current investment provider to complete the required documentation. This is expected to be a lengthy process.

Governors thanked TT for his support and the time he has dedicated to progressing this matter.

17 | Policies/Guidance for review include (on Gov Hub):

Lettings Policy: EB advised governors that the lettings fees have been updated and an evacuation plan added.
Governors queried whether a clause should be included to exclude liability for loss of injury. BR agreed to clarify whether any hirers use the HCC insurance as any clause would need to also reflect this. 

Q – Who needs to read this policy?
A – While the federation does not usually hire the premises for one off lettings, any hirer would be required to read this policy prior to hiring the premises.

Q – The hiring costs have increased during weekends and school holiday hirings except the playground at Victoria, is there a reason for this?
A – The playground is rarely hired out, so it felt appropriate to keep it the same.

Code of Conduct – parents, carers and visitors replaced by the new Disruptive Behaviour policy 
The previous Code of Conduct for Parents, Carers and Visitors has been replaced by the new Disruptive Behaviour Policy. BR explained that she has used this policy before and developed it with the HCC legal team, ensuring it reflects current harassment legislation. She advised that it is a very robust document and recommended that governors adopt it. The policy addresses issues such as harassment and intimidation.

Governors discussed the section relating to derogatory comments on social media. They considered how to achieve the right balance, recognising that stakeholders should be free to comment about the school and to raise appropriate challenge, while also defining what constitutes inappropriate or harmful criticism.

BR noted that if a parent was overtly critical LF, LD and BR would always seek to approach the parent directly to resolve matters. HCC has been clear that schools should not be subject to unreasonable or abusive criticism

TT expressed concern about how the policy balances this with freedom of speech.
NB-W commented that the degree of criticism, including both content and frequency, must be considered. BR added that issues also arise when a parent is critical of staff members on platforms such as WhatsApp, Governors agreed this was unacceptable.

BR agreed to review this point and the policy will be reviewed again at the next FGB meeting.

EB requested that CW update the numbering on the policy and remove the requirement for the COG to sign the document.

Attendance Policy 

EB confirmed the only change was to LD’s surname. 

It was noted by governors that there was no reference to the rule requiring children to remain off school for 48 hours after being sick. It was suggested that this should be included.BR agreed to review this, Governors were happy to approve the current policy.

Attendance Policy V: No changes

Governors approved the policy for Thomas Coram and Victoria.

Prevent Policy:  Governors approved the policy

Pay Policy

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

Minutes of the FGB Meeting of Governors held on 

Wednesday 10th September 2025 at Thomas Coram

Chaired by Elaine Bunn

Present:

There being no further business the meeting closed at 9.15pm

Ms R Roberts (BR, Exec Head)
Mrs L Daily (LD, Head of Thomas Coram)
Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria)
Mrs E Bunn (EB, Chair)
Mrs S Giles (SG)

Mr M Vibert (MV)
Mrs C Cartwright (CC)

Apologies received: Mrs K Hennessey (KH), Mrs S Holmes (SH), Mr T Trailor (TT), Mrs T Brown (TB)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional | Apologies received: Mrs K Hennessey (KH), Mrs S Holmes (SH), Mr T Trailor (TT), Mrs T Brown (TB)

1 | Introduction

Welcome, Opening Prayers and Confidentiality Reminder

Reconfirm strategy meeting objectives

Governors agreed the focus is to align objectives of the Governing board with the objectives of the Federation.

2 | Reflection on last year and previous goals.
EB welcomed CC and LPr and thanked everyone for their commitment and emphasised the importance of the school’s culture in supporting the Federation.

Governors agreed that the excellent results from both schools should be celebrated, as they reflect the dedication of staff. In addition, Victoria have been invited to be a Champion School by Little Wandle which is excellent achievement. 

Governors acknowledged strong recruitment, noting only one Governor vacancy remains and that the board has a broad and robust skill set.

Review of last year’s priorities for Governors
Governors reviewed last year’s priorities and agreed:
Communication strategy: working group has been very effective and it was agreed the committee members would remain the same for 25-26 (MV, MT, ID and TT) although TT has now stepped back from this committee!
Governor visits effectiveness: significant work has led to more effective visits, with most staff providing positive feedback. It was agreed that further refinements are needed, including clearly identifying visit objectives for governors and supporting them to understand how best to achieve those objectives
Training: SH has championed governor development, ensuring everyone is up to date with recommended training. Moving forward BR and EB proposed governors could utilise the learning links on the NGA and governors agreed they would benefit from BR signposting specific areas.
Church Distinctiveness: Christian identity strengthened including commissioning and installing two new murals.
MV highlighted that TC had achieved a distinction in Green Schools which governors agreed is an excellent achievement.

3 | Review GB structure- ensuring effectiveness							
Instrument of Governance- EB reminded governors of the Governing board structure
16 Governors (1 Exec Head, 1 staff, 2 Co-opted, 9 Foundation Governors, 1 LA, 2 parent)
Changes to structure of Governing Board
Lucy Hall (LH) now known as Lucy Daily (LD)
MT staying as Associate Member, leaves 1 vacancy now and another when KH leaves
TB has been voted in as a Foundation governor and therefore she is no longer an Associate Member and will serve a term of 4 years.

Governors elected and confirmed the following roles (see Governor Hub for full structure):
Chair of Governors - EB
Vice-Chair of Governors – TT
Chair of Resources – TT
Vice-Chair of Resources - MT

Anthony Boden (AB) as an Associate Member as sustainability adviser.

Code of Conduct 2025 – review and approve
Governors approved the amendment. CW to upload the document for governors to sign on Governor Hub.
Governor Induction and Support
EB highlighted the document to new governors and the importance of reviewing the contents. The onboarding process can be lengthy, governors agreed that clearer signposting of training platforms would be appreciated.
Governance professional update
CW advised all compliance checks to be completed by 30 September and will email governors with instructions. The skills audit has been replaced by a more user-friendly Governance Effectiveness Tool.

4 | School’s priorities for the year ahead

Victoria achievements and priorities of School Improvement Plan (SIP) 
Governors congratulated LF on the following achievements at Victoria last year:
Becoming of champion of Little Wandle – LF stated the success would not happen without an effective team
Successful collaborative working across both schools for subject leaders
Effective implementation of Kindness and Spiritual Ambassadors
The Stay and Play initiative was successful, leading to increased nursery admissions. In addition, a grant was secured to improve the provision.

LF shared the following SIP Priorities with governors:
1 Foundation Subject Assessments – used effectively to ensure children can retain and retrieve core knowledge – children should demonstrate articulate learning as they progress through the school
2 Oracy across the curriculum – developing skills from Nursery and Reception where some pupils have struggled with communication skills by supporting children to become confident speakers with oracy playing a key role.
3 Writing fluency – developing strong foundations using the early writing framework, understanding how to support pupils, including developing fine motor skills

Q – Do we have access to a Speech and Language (S&L) therapist and do staff have any S&L training?
A – There are various accessible programmes, staff have not had specific S&L training. The initial step is to conduct an audit to assess and identify needs

Q – Why are we seeing increasing challenges with communication skills?
A – Research indicates that the growing use of mobile devices is having an effect on fundamental communication skills, making it vital to tackle this in the Early Years to lessen the impact.

Q – Are parents supported in reading with their children?
A – Yesterday a PowerPoint was presented to parents, explaining when to read to children and how to listen to them read, this received positive feedback from parents.

Q – What are the outcome measures for priority 1?
A – Working in collaboration with the assessment team at Hertfordshire to develop knowledge organisers and teacher activities, including targeted questioning to assess children’s learning (e.g., identifying how many children can recall and explain five key facts about a topic). Learning is measured both during and after activities. In addition, partnered with a Herts Teaching and Learning Adviser to support a specific teacher in driving the curriculum and to work with ECTs to strengthen assessment practice.

Q – Are parents aware of what the children are learning so they could support their understanding at home?
A – A curriculum letter is sent home each term outlining the areas of learning to be covered.

Q – Regarding priority 2, are there any smart goals for assessing effectiveness?
A – An initial audit must be completed to identify specific criteria for a working group to consider. Smart goals will be agreed following this assessment.


TC achievements and priorities of School Improvement Plan (SIP) 

LD was congratulated by the Governors on the following successes at TC last year:
Fantastic SATS results, all above national and Hertfordshire averages. Governors agreed the additional teacher in Year 6 for Maths and English contributed towards the success, this has now been expanded to Year 5
Excellent Multiplication check results with an increasing two-year trend
The new writing scheme introduced in January has boosted teacher confidence and strengthened children’s ownership of their writing
The introduction of Pixl assessments in Years 3-6 has supported child development
Year 6 successfully raised £800 via their enterprise activities

LD advised governors that SIP priorities 1 and 2 are the same as Victoria’s.
Priority 3 -The aim is to improve children’s accuracy in key mathematical knowledge to strengthen reasoning and understanding. With support from the new Maths Co-ordinator the first step will be to identify strong areas and development needs via a learning walk.

Q – After reviewing maths, how will you measure progress?
A – Monitoring key priorities within lessons, such as the use of concrete resources, establishing guidelines for a working wall, and benefiting from continued guidance from the Herts Teaching and Learning Adviser.

Q – When you talk about accuracy can we benchmark against other schools nationally and locally?
A – As accuracy relates to knowledge of key number facts, external comparisons are limited, so attention is directed towards consistency throughout the school

Q Can you explain assessments in writing?
A Due to low writing attainment across the school, moderation was carried out in the Spring and Summer terms. Prescriptive outcomes have been set for each child. Whole-school assessment will include children writing a letter to their teacher to assess key aspects of their writing.

Exec Head’s Review of Federation Improvement Plan (FIP) priorities 
BR shared a summary of the key priorities of the FIP with governors:

Priority 1 – Building on existing practice to develop the following four pillars:
Educational Excellence
Happiness
Berkhamsted Community
Sustainability

Priority 2 - Accelerating pupil progress by creating equity for the vulnerable pupils (VIP’s) across the Federation
Shifting staff mindset to ensure vulnerable children (VIP’s) have access to necessary resources
The Federation will be working with 21 schools across Hertfordshire working on supporting the VIP’s which includes allocating a specific adult to each vulnerable child.
Using a spreadsheet developed by Hertfordshire County Council to identify key areas of vulnerability and providing bespoke support to enable them to move forward
Developing a consistent approach across the Federation, to support children returning from an absence, ensuring they feel valued and missed, supporting a sense of belonging

Priority 3 Distinctive Christian Character
Forming a working group to review all aspects of Christian Distinctiveness - monitoring whole school collective worship and asking governors to be involved in assessing this.

Priority 4 - Careers programme across the federation
Supporting pupils to gain an understanding of potential future careers from EY to Year 6

2024-25 Achievements across the Federation
Extensive work on embedding the school’s vision and values with children, supporting all pupils to articulate them confidently.
Significant development of the RE curriculum and collective worship.
Creation of a robust 5-year strategic plan.
Enhancement of appraisal processes to ensure accountability for all staff.
Strong pupil outcomes across both schools.
Reviewed financial allocation to provide additional interventions and small-group support.
Effective marketing initiatives, particularly at Victoria.

Governors agreed the FIP was robust and contained SMART deliverables.


Q – VIP’s formal assessments and diagnosis can be challenging to obtain, how is the Federation supporting children with suspected conditions?
A -  Prior to formal diagnosis the SENDCo will be involved with the child, supporting them with interventions. All classes have consistent resources, for example all classes are dyslexia friendly.

Ofsted update training

To keep governors informed, LD agreed to share four recent Ofsted updates. BR highlighted the importance of governors understanding their role within the Federation, which included an in-depth understanding of Ofsted expectations.

5 | Round table discussion on school priorities and alignment of governing board priorities:

Governors split into small groups to discuss the following areas and agreed the following:

Are they the right priorities
Governors believe the highlighted priorities effectively support the development of the Federation. Having contributed to these priorities, they consider them well-aligned, balancing educational objectives with appropriate challenge to drive ongoing improvement across the Federation.

How can we as governors support the schools in achieving their goals

Governors are assigned to specific areas of the 5-year plan, with ongoing visits supporting continued progress toward these goals.

What should our goals as a governing board be:

Ofsted training to identify key focusses for governors
Year 1 priorities of the strategic plan will be a major focus, with all governors assigned specific roles to support its implementation
Refining Governor visit structure to ensure they are effective
Succession planning including ongoing training, ensuring roles are filled to support continuity


d. Success criteria

Governors agreed to review the success criteria for their goals at the next FGB meeting.

6 | Personal planning exercise

Each governor created a governor personal action plan detailing how they will support the governing board and school priorities.

7 | Each governor to present back their personal action plan highlighting their goals and priorities for the year ahead:

Governors agreed the following personal actions:
MV – Marketing: continue sustaining progress and long-term sustainability, driving successful admission numbers at Victoria. Admissions: Receive training to support processes. Pupil and staff discipline: Monitor systems to ensure effectiveness. Complaints: Manage in a sensitive and professional manner.
ID – Safeguarding: Acting as new safeguarding lead; to receive support from LD and LF and complete governor safeguarding training within the first term. Meet with DSLs across the federation. Curriculum: Validate implementation of new phonics and writing schemes, meet termly with literacy leads in both schools to deepen understanding. Marketing: Participate in the marketing committee to develop skills in publishing and data analysis
SO – Collective worship: Continue embedding work and invest additional time, following last year’s sabbatical. Stuart left at 9pm
NB-W – School understanding: Build knowledge following time spent with SENDCo’s; observe provision for EHCPs and review how schools meet pupil needs. Review staff training scope and provisions. Leadership: Shadow KH to take over P&C Chair. Classroom links: Review consistency of learning and vocabulary teaching. As Foundation Governor support the school’s Christian Distinctiveness, potentially strengthening links with Sunnyside Church. Discuss with SLT developing a Christian Distinctiveness committee to monitor and review performance, drawing on previous governor experience
MT – Marketing: Support SLT using newsletters and the church community; consider training in school marketing
CC – School visits: Aim to visit the school weekly to gain insight, linked to a class so teachers feel supported. Suggested activities include assemblies, small groups at lunchtime, collective worship, and learning walks. Follow-up via email to arrange visits 

TB, KH, SH, and TT - Absent

Governors agreed it was a valuable exercise and provided an opportunity to focus on their own development.

8 | Group discussion on the individual action plans

4 | HR

Confirmation of staff performance appraisal process and consideration of recommendations for pay reviews, including UPS applications

All staff appraisals have been completed. BR shared anonymised appraisal documentation. Staff highlighted in yellow are already at the top of their pay scale; those highlighted in green are recommended for progression.

Q: Were there any conflicting comments from staff?
A: No. As part of the review process, all staff were offered professional development opportunities and access to mental health support, reinforcing that they are valued members of the school community.

Q: What type of responses are typically received regarding mental health support?
A: Most staff decline support, but they are encouraged to return if their circumstances change. A robust referral system is in place.

Q: Why are some staff both at the top of scale and recorded as ‘partially met’?
A: There are no significant concerns with individual staff performance. In these cases, mid-cycle role changes meant original targets could not be fully met.

Governors approved the proposed scale-point increases for those highlighted in green, confirming these costs are within budget.

BR confirmed that no UPS applications were submitted this cycle.



Early Career Teacher support 
LF reported that two ECTs remain at Victoria. One is due to complete their induction by Christmas. Both are proactive in seeking advice, accessing support, and visiting other schools to enhance their practice. Both are on track with no concerns. There are currently no ECTs at TC. Governors agreed that this was an excellent outcome.

Staffing updates 
Maternity cover appointments have been made at Victoria; three strong candidates have been secured. A comparison between agency costs and direct employment was carried out as part of the recruitment process, and the difference in cost was minimal. Governors agreed that in the current education recruitment crisis, this was a very positive outcome.

At TC, a one-to-one support staff member has been appointed who will work across both Victoria and TC.

•  Staff Absence and Trends 2024–25
Absence data can only be produced on a February-to-February basis. Governors reviewed data and queried the following points:

Q: Why is Victoria’s average absence higher than TC’s?
A: Victoria has a smaller workforce, so individual absences have a greater proportional impact. Return-to-work meetings and Occupational Health referrals are completed where appropriate.

Q: Is there a trend in mental health-related absence?
A: Issues are predominantly individual and linked to external factors rather than workplace pressures. The current pattern remains consistent with previous data.

Q: Are any incentives offered for 100% attendance—for example, time off in lieu?
A: BR will review potential incentives, as this may have a positive impact.

Governors agreed that whilst a review of the information was very useful, updated data should be reviewed in the summer term, as the current dataset is nine months old.

BR also noted that sickness insurance schemes are in place and that payments will be received for eligible absence claims. These payments do not yet appear in the budget monitor, as the exact amounts have not been confirmed. | LP/BR

5 | Finance
P6 Monitor 
Governors reviewed the monitor and questions were invited.

Q: At TC there is £13,000 of SEN income that has not been received. What is the reason for this?
A: One child was incorrectly banded and another has left, resulting in the shortfall.

Q: Agency supply costs at TC have increased by £17,000. What has caused this? Is the phasing correct and is all of this budgeted to be spent in Period 12?
A: Unexpected absences have resulted in an increase in supply costs. The associated cost has been allocated across the year rather than being concentrated in Period 12.
Q: There are three new staff appointed to the ASC at Victoria. Is there additional income to support this?
A: Additional revenue is expected, but we have taken a prudent approach. Increased sickness levels and the appointment of a manager have resulted in higher expenditure. An additional staff member has been recruited to ensure consistent cover during absences and while this will not generate additional revenue, it ensures a reliable service for parents.

6 | SFVS Audit Update
