7 | Health and Safety update
The quinquennial report for Victoria has been completed, at a cost of £4,500, which has highlighted a number of actions. Health & Safety inspections are scheduled for 21st and 28th November.

Q: Has the report highlighted a higher volume of actions than expected?
A: The report informs bids for work to enable schools to request funding from the Diocese. Approximately 90% of the identified work is decorative or superficial. Items classified as D1 are currently being costed, as these are a higher priority. 

BR confirmed that actions arising from the report are being addressed and will be shared with MT, who will provide feedback in the next Resources meeting.

In addition, fire safety audits have been completed at both schools. Following the audits eight staff members have completed fire warden training. | MT

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

 Minutes of the Meeting of the Admissions Committee held on 
Thursday 19th June 2025
In Person at Victoria School
Present:	
Mrs E Bunn (EB) (Stand-in Chair)
Mrs L Freeman
Miss L Hill

Mrs B Roberts (BR, Executive Head)
Fr S Owen (SO)


1
Welcome and confidentiality reminder
EB opened the meeting and reminded the committee about confidentiality.

2.45
2
Conflicts of Interests and apologies for absence.
No conflict of interest, apologies of absence received and accepted from 
Mr N Goss


3
Consideration of pupil repeating a year – see document on Governor Hub – Continuation of consideration process started 16.06.25

Governors reviewed the notes of the Occupational Therapist (OT) report dated 27/2/25 and agreed that the content of those notes had not persuaded governors that the child repeating Reception year was in his best interests.

BR confirmed that the child’s teacher does not feel him repeating Reception year would be the best option for him. BR believes that it could be detrimental to his social and emotional wellbeing than transitioning into year 1 with his peers.  She added that the class teacher had confirmed that there was nothing contained within the notes of the OT report, in terms of interventions and support, that could not be offered to the child in year 1. 

LF said that there would be additional transition arrangements and support put in place for him, to ensure that his introduction to year 1 was the best possible experience.

SO observed that the impact on the child’s social and emotional wellbeing of being held back a year could have a disadvantageous effect, as this would be the third set of peers in a year. As the concern is over his social and emotional wellbeing, as well as his academic achievement, staying with his friends that he has made in Reception would be the best support for him.  

Governors unanimously decided that the child will benefit most from transitioning into year 1 rather than repeating Reception, and that the parents should be informed at the earliest opportunity of this decision.

It was decided that a letter confirming this decision should be sent out before the end of Friday 20th June 2025.


7
Meeting dates 2025

8
Any other business

No further business was raised.

It was agreed that the meeting had been conducted in line with our vision and values.


9
Action points
EB to prepare and circulate minutes of this meeting for approval by 20th June 2025.
Letter confirming outcome of decision to be sent to parents before the end of 20th June 2025.

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

Minutes of the Resources Meeting of Governors held on 

Wednesday 8th October 2025 at Thomas Coram

Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria)

      Mr T Trailor (TT) | Mrs C Cartwright (CC)
Mr A Boden (AB)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional and Ms L Penny (LP) Finance Lead for the Federation | Apologies received: Mr M Thomson (MT), Mrs L Preston (LPr) and Mr M Vibert (MV)

1 | Introduction

4 | Agree minutes of meeting (on Gov Hub)
Minutes of 14th May 2025 approved by Governors

Q – Are the pupil numbers correct?
A -  At TC there are now 3 children being home educated, so the pupil number is 339

Q - Are there any safeguarding concerns regarding the pupils being home educated?
A -  No, all required safeguarding paperwork has been completed.

Matters arising from 14th May 2025:
TR will collate the results from the Wellbeing survey and create an action plan to share at the FGB on 2nd July - completed
BR will update governors on the variation in staffing costs in 26/27, by 16th May 2025 completed via email
BR and LP to review and update risk register and send to TT for initial review, submitting to governors by the end of the summer term completed
LP will update the H&S document to include LF as the mental health lead for Victoria, by 10th June 2025 completed

5 | Finance (documents on Governor Hub)
Budget vs actual to date 
Confirm audit of private fund and governor fund and actions
Letting income
Schedule of Financial Delegation
P5 Monitors
Review M&G trust monies Victoria

LP invited questions on the various financial reports.

Bank Accounts
Q - Governors noted that the bank account balances are lower than in the previous year and requested clarification.
A - It was confirmed that the figures represent a snapshot taken on a specific day. The school’s RAG rating is green, and the monitoring report provides a more accurate reflection of the overall financial position.

Decorating Costs
Q - Governors queried the absence of decorating expenditure in the budget.
A - It was confirmed that the costs were covered from the TC Fund account rather than the main school budget.

Governor Account Balance
Q - Governors observed that the Governor account balance has been increasing year on year and asked whether the funds are earmarked.
A - The funds are increasing as the investment returns are currently higher than governor expenditure. The funds are not earmarked and are available for use – any proposals are very welcome. It was however noted that the investment funds are currently held in the names of two priests. The Finance Governor is investigating options to transfer the funds into the school’s name, as governors do not currently have access to the trust.

Expenditure Variance Between TC and Victoria
Q - Governors asked why more money had been spent from the TC Governor account than from the Victoria account.
A - It was confirmed that spending is usually split approximately 50/50 between the two accounts, although small variances may occur. The main driver for the difference is likely to be the returns produced from the underlying investments, rather than from the expenditure split.

Lettings Income
Q - Governors requested an update on lettings income against the budget.
A - It was reported TC has met its lettings budget target, while Victoria has not yet achieved its projected income. The main challenges for Victoria include limited parking and the absence of a site manager outside of normal hours.

Schedule of Financial Delegation 
Governors approved the Schedule of Financial Delegation.

P5 Monitor
Governors reviewed the P5 monitor and sought clarification on staffing expenditure, specifically the £72,000 allocated for two teachers and a £41,000 reduction in TA spending. Governors asked whether the school remains able to appoint the teachers included in the budget, including the full-time Year 5 teacher.
.
BR confirmed that one teacher returning from maternity leave resumed at 0.6 FTE, resulting in a budget saving. Recruitment for a second teacher was unsuccessful; instead, an almost full-time additional TA has been appointed to support Years 3, 4, and 5. BR advised that this strategic decision allows for greater flexibility and targeted pupil interventions. In addition, the budget had initially allowed for several one-to-one support staff, but the actual need was lower than anticipated. 

LD advised governors that some pupils from Swing Gate were initially assessed as requiring one-to-one support but did not ultimately need it. Agency staff were also engaged as required (shown in E26). LD also noted that the budget was set early in the year before the final cohort information was available. BR agreed with LD stating that retaining TAs within classrooms has proven a more effective approach, avoiding the need to reallocate staff across year groups.

Q - Governors sought assurance that the level of intervention support remains appropriate.
A – LD confirmed confidence in the current provision, noting smaller class sizes and well-planned interventions will positively impact pupil outcomes
.
Q - Governors asked whether there were any further priorities for investment.
A - It was reported that an additional teacher works one morning per week with Year 4 pupils. BR confirmed that the current staffing structure is effective, particularly supporting the focus on disadvantaged pupils. Governors were reminded that, in light of reducing pupil numbers, it is essential to remain mindful of budget constraints and therefore the positive impact on the budget would support the strategic direction of the school.

Q - Governors also noted an increase in TA numbers at Victoria and sought clarification.
A - It was confirmed that this is due to maintaining two classes per year group, and therefore retaining existing TA positions.





Nursery and ASC Update
LF advised governors that Nursery pupil numbers increased from 17 at the start of last year to 23 at year end, and currently stand at 32, with 34 expected by Christmas. Due to recent changes in EYFS staffing ratios, this presents some operational challenges but confirmed that the higher numbers will generate additional income.

LD advised governors that at TC, the After School Club (ASC) attendance has risen significantly, with up to 78 children attending on two evenings per week.

M&G Income
BR advised governors that an email was received from the School Building Officer confirming that £13,000 had been received and was being held by the Diocese as custodians of these funds for the federation and governors should decide which investment option to proceed with from:

Ethical investment via CCLA
Review alternative investment companies

Q - Governors asked what restrictions apply to the use of these funds.
A - It was confirmed that the parameters are not yet known. It was agreed that an initial meeting should be arranged with the Diocese advisors to discuss investment options and how to incorporate the Governors’ account.

TT suggested arranging a joint meeting to discuss both the M&G funds and the Governors’ account investments.

6 | HR Update

Staffing Overview
Governors received an update on staffing in the After School Club (ASC). BR advised that staffing costs have been increased due to sickness absence and maternity cover. An ASC manager has been appointed, and additional staff have been recruited to ensure sufficient capacity, as it can be challenging to find short notice cover. LD stated that the new arrangements are reported to be working effectively.

LD advised that additional external lighting had been installed at TC to enable children in the ASC to play outdoors, as the indoor rooms are relatively small for the increased numbers attending.

Leadership Structure
BR advised Governors that Lisa Williamson (Assistant headteacher at TC) will be leaving at Christmas. Recruitment for this post is being considered for September 2026. BR and LD will review and determine the nature of the role before recruitment begins.

Q - Governors asked whether there had been any consideration to appoint a Deputy Headteacher versus an Assistant Headteacher, and what the financial implications might be.
A - It was confirmed that a Deputy Headteacher would command a higher salary. Additionally, within a Head of School structure, an Assistant Head role is more appropriate and maintains consistency across both schools.
Q - Governors also noted that the departing staff member is currently the Mental Health Lead and asked how this responsibility will be managed.
A - It was confirmed that existing staff have either completed, or are currently undertaking, the necessary training to cover this area. It was further noted that appointing a non-teaching Assistant Headteacher would not be financially viable and would be considered during the recruitment process.

Confirm staff register of pecuniary interest 
BR confirmed that 85% of staff have completed the pecuniary interest form, with one member of staff declaring a pecuniary interest.

Staff Communication Survey
Governors were updated on the communication survey feedback, which has been shared with governors via Governor Hub. BR advised that both schools undertook a significant review of communication, and responses have been provided to staff outlining what was said, what actions have been taken, and next steps.
A joint staff newsletter has been introduced, covering TC and Victoria, to celebrate successes and improve transparency. Increased communication also includes updates on staff absences and cover arrangements.

Q - Governors asked whether there had been more negative feedback from Victoria compared to TC.
A - It was noted that this is difficult to measure, as Victoria has a smaller staff team, meaning a few comments can have a greater perceived impact.

EB highlighted several positive outcomes from the survey, including:
Strong sense of care and mutual support among staff
Kind and supportive line management
Positive teamwork observed
Very positive feedback regarding the recent inset day

Governors commended how the leadership team addressed and responded to staff feedback.

7 | Premises, H&S (documents on Governor Hub)

Health & Safety Inspections
LP advised Governors that the Health and Safety inspections for both TC and Victoria took place during the summer term. All documentation relating to the inspections has been made available on Governor Hub.

Q - Governors asked whether the fire brigade inspections had been completed.
A - It was confirmed that inspections were carried out at both schools.

Governors were advised by LP that it is useful to review the summer inspection reports in the Autumn term, to reflect on progress and any outstanding actions, therefore always reviewing actions from the previous term.

Q – Governors queried whether there should be a further Legionella risk assessment commissioned.
A – It was confirmed that as no changes have occurred, no further action was required at this time.
BR advised governors that an asbestos survey had been conducted at TC and they were awaiting the full report.


Staff Wellbeing and Stress Management
Q - Governors enquired whether stress and wellbeing are included within the risk assessment process and how these areas are being addressed.
A - It was confirmed that wellbeing is discussed as part of both full and interim appraisals. In addition, some staff have had specific meetings regarding wellbeing and have been signposted to the school’s insurer, who provides an employee wellbeing package, particularly for those with mental health concerns.

BR advised governors that TR has identified volunteers in both schools to review and develop the Mental Health and Wellbeing Charter.


Accidents and Incident Reporting
Q - Governors asked how information on accidents and incidents is shared with governors.
A - It was confirmed that the Senior Leadership Team at both schools regularly review and monitor incident trends using the Medical Tracker system. Where trends are identified, appropriate action is taken. This information has been shared with the Safeguarding Governor, demonstrating how medical tracker works.

LD advised governors that at TC, the artificial grass surface has become sharp in areas and will be replaced. There were also three recent incidents involving the adventure trail, resulting in three children attending hospital as a result of the injuries. Consequently, the adventure trail has been temporarily closed while pupils are retrained on safe usage. All incidents have been reported to Hertfordshire County Council (HCC).

Q - Governors asked whether the medical tracker data could be shared with governors?
A – BR confirmed that this could be reviewed during the H&S governor visit, reviewing statistics and identifying any recurring themes. 

TT also requested that where it was noted on the H&S report, that there were some incidents but that statistics on these hadn’t been shared with the governors it should state ‘no’ rather than N/A. LP and BR agreed this would be amended on future reports.

8 | GDPR Compliance Update
Governors received an update on GDPR compliance from BR. It was reported that a data breach occurred due to an email being sent to the wrong parent. Appropriate actions were taken to address the incident in line with GDPR procedures.

BR also advised that the federation has changed its Data Protection Officer (DPO) to an HfL adviser. While this provides expertise, it is not a like-for-like replacement, and some additional internal training may be required. This change has resulted in a significant cost saving.
Governors were also informed by BR that two subject access requests from parents of ex-pupils (one at each school) have been received and successfully processed.

Probationary Policy – EB suggested that additional training may be required, should governors be involved in a probationary hearing
Charging Remissions Policy

[SOURCE: Resources Minutes 2025-05-14.docx | Ofsted 26 Victoria /Minutes/Resources/2024-25 | Modified: 2025-09-28]

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

Minutes of the Resources Meeting of Governors held on 

Wednesday 14th May 2025 – Thomas Coram

Chaired by Bev Jullien

Present:

There being no further business the meeting closed at 8.40pm 

Ms R Roberts (BR, Exec Head)
Mrs L Hill (LH, Head of Thomas Coram)
Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria)
Mrs E Bunn (EB, Chair)
Mr T Trailor (TT) | Mrs V Harris (VH)
Mrs B Jullien (BJ)
Mrs S Holmes (SH)
Mrs N Boddam-Whetham (NB-W)

Michael Vibert (MV) – remote for budget approval, left meeting at 8pm
Tracey Brown (TB) -   remote for budget approval, left meeting at 7.50pm

The meeting was FGB quorate, therefore budget approval took place during this meeting.

Apologies received: Mr M Thomson (MT), Kate Hennessy (KH), Nick Goss (NG) Stuart Owen (SO) and Stacey Giles (SG)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional and Liz Penny (LP) Finance Assistant | Michael Vibert (MV) – remote for budget approval, left meeting at 8pm
Tracey Brown (TB) -   remote for budget approval, left meeting at 7.50pm

The meeting was FGB quorate, therefore budget approval took place during this meeting.

Apologies received: Mr M Thomson (MT), Kate Hennessy (KH), Nick Goss (NG) Stuart Owen (SO) and Stacey Giles (SG)

Also in attendance: Mrs C Wallis (CW) Governance Professional and Liz Penny (LP) Finance Assistant

1 | Welcome, Opening Prayers and Confidentiality Reminder
BJ opened the meeting at 7pm and led the Resources committee in prayer. Colleagues were reminded of the confidentiality of the meeting.

2 | Conflicts of Interest and Apologies for Absence
Apologies were received and accepted by Governors for MT, KH, NG, SO and SG

No conflicts of interest declared.

AOB – none raised

3 | Part 1 and 2 minutes of resources meeting of 12th February 2025: approved

Matters arising:
TR to forward wellbeing action plan prior to the end of term – LP confirmed that all staff responses had been received with the majority of staff stating that they did not feel overwhelmed by their work levels. TR will collate the information and create an action plan to share at the FGB at July.
BR to submit the SFVS to EB, BJ and TT to consider. Following this review BR to upload to Governor Hub for approval at the March FGB Completed
BR to consider how to implement governor finance monitoring six times a year and propose at next FGB - Completed
BR to share Wi-Fi quotes with governors by 14th February Completed
CW to add Risk Register review of Section 1 - Strategic and Reputational Risk to the next Resources meeting. The risk register should be a standing item for each Resources meeting Completed
CW to add policy approval process to the next FGB agenda – To be reviewed 21st May 2025 | TR

4 | Finance 

BR gave thanks to LP, LH and LF for their hard work contributing to the budget setting process.

BR confirmed that there are 4 accounts for each school:
General account
Fund account 
Devolved Formula Capital (DFC)
Governors account

End of year accounts
BR presented an overview of the 24/25-year end accounts (see PowerPoint presentation on Governor Hub). This included BR advising Governors of the following information:

Victoria

A significant expenditure under the DFC was the installation of new toilets at Victoria.
LF secured a wraparound grant for £11,000, which will be paid over 2 years. This will be used to purchase additional resources and provide support for those children with SEND and train staff to effectively meet the needs of the children.
There was a reduction in UIFSM expenditure due to a high number of children having meals on census day, which was not consistent with meal levels throughout the year.
There was an increase in wraparound care over the year, providing an additional £29,000.
The year end was significantly higher than expected in the previous monitor, which has positively impacted the 25/26 budget. The year end carried forward into 25/26 was £396,101.

Q – Why is there a significant increase in period 12?
A - There are various assumptions that are considered when monitoring throughout the year and the actual outturn is not always realised until the final month of the financial year (March). For example: it was anticipated that the utility budgets and subject budgets would be fully spent, however that was not the case. 

Q – Should there be further investment in Safeguarding in the new budget?
A - The decision to continue to use CPOMS provides an extremely effective system that allows staff to record any incident, which alerts the DSL’s. All incidents are reviewed and appropriately managed. 

Q - How often do DSL’s meet? 
A – BR confirmed DSL’s meet weekly. DSL’s review every CPOMS entry and meet to discuss any significant incidents recorded and agree appropriate action. LH advised that she receives approximately 50 CPOMS alerts every day. 

VH advised that in addition, she carries out a termly governor safeguarding visit where the data is analysed using various reports to review the number and range of safeguarding incidents raised by staff. Any personal data and detailed information is not shared with VH, in accordance with GDPR.

Thomas Coram

There have not been any significant purchases through the Fund account in 24/25, as BR knew there would be a larger expense in 25/26. The Fund account will be used to invest in a new Wi-Fi system and support the 
re-decoration of various areas of the school.
There has been a significant increase in the number of attendees in the wraparound care, providing an additional £34,500, this has supported the costs in running the childcare provision.
The telephone system proved cheaper to install than budgeted.
There was also a reduction in various staffing costs such as admin, support staff and teacher costs.
The year end carried forward into 25/26 is £346,485. This was significantly higher than expected in the previous monitor, which has positively impacted the 25/26 budget, which has been due to similar factors that have affected the year end at Victoria, such as a reduction in utility costs, as well as an increase in Additional Targeted Funding (ATF) and SEND funding due to further successful EHCP applications towards the end of the financial year.

For further detail on the Victoria and Thomas Coram year end accounts, the following documents have been shared on Governor Hub:

Budget V actual V committed accruals 
Year-end income from lettings 
Year-end bank accounts 
Cross charging between schools
Monitor 

2025-26 budget 
BR explained the process of budget setting starts in January with BR, LH and LF reviewing staffing structures and considering curriculum priorities and focuses for the next year. In addition, BR and LP meet AT to review the premises priorities. BR advised that the HCC budget guidance, which was shared on Governor Hub, is followed including the assumptions. The contracts are also reviewed, identifying cost savings and any potential increases during contract renewals.

BR advised that when considering the budget, various factors were considered, including potential changes in income associated with pupil numbers, lettings, Sports Premium, SEND funding and the wraparound provision. BR advised that she has been conservative and realistic in her forecast of income, avoiding overly optimistic assumptions.

On the advice from Financial Services, Sports Premium remains in the budget across all years, however whilst schools have been assured funding will remain in place for the 25/26 academic year this may be withdrawn in the near future.

BR explained the impact of pupil numbers on the budget, with each pupil attributing approximately £4,000pa.

BR advised that a significant proportion of each school budget was allocated to staffing and after required expenditure such as utilities, insurance and maintenance costs have been deducted there are minimal funds to spend across other areas.

BR presented an overview of the budgets, shown in the PowerPoint presentation on Governor Hub, which included the following information:

Thomas Coram

BR highlighted that the whole school pupil numbers are budgeted to be 343 in summer 2025, increasing to 346 in the Autumn and Spring term, with a slight increase in Autumn 2026, then falling to 338 in Autumn 2027. Despite some year groups having pupil numbers in the 80s, there remains 3 class teachers in each year group.
Despite not all classes being full, TC does admit pupils throughout the year that are transferring from other schools. In last 3 weeks there have been 6 new children join across the school
There are additional one to ones in the budget to support children accessing the curriculum. There are currently 14 children with EHCP’s, and this number is increasing across all schools in Hertfordshire; having the support in place for them is vital.
The booster groups for core subjects have been very successful so in 3 out of 4 year groups there is an additional teacher allocated in the budget for September. The school is also recruiting for staff to carry our more interventions to support pupil outcomes.
When reviewing the income from wraparound care there has been consideration of a fall in pupil numbers therefore a conservative level of income has been included.
There are contracts that will be reviewed this year, for example the cleaning contract has seen a significant price increase of approximately 11%, which is included in the budget however, it is expected that the outturn will be lower if we move to an alternative provider/negotiate the price.
Under E19, £6000 has been budgeted for curriculum resources, this allows for additional funds to be allocated to the School Development Plan. 

Q - How confident are you that the budget allocated to E19 is enough?
A - All subject leaders request a budget and the priorities in each subject area are considered when allocating the funds. There is also a contingency within the £6000 to allow for further unexpected curricular costs.

Q – The Planned Supply costs (E26) are high at £35,405, have you considered recruiting one additional staff member that could be used across the federation?
A – There has been consideration of recruiting a staff member to provide regular supply, however due to the range of roles, age groups and requirements, along with the frequency of supply needed across both schools, one person would not suffice and therefore the decision was made to liaise with agencies to provide the relevant supply staff as this is also more cost effective. LH advised that she provides an increasing level of cover herself and whilst this is challenging, this also reduces the supply cover costs.

Q - Can we access the pupil: staff ratio?
A - This information is shared in the benchmarking data; it will highlight the school being higher than comparable schools as we employ more staff than some schools however, that is the Federation’s strategy to support children to access the curriculum in the most effective way.

Q - How do you make SEND provision in the budget for those who have not joined the school yet?
A - You cannot anticipate how many in-year admissions the school will receive and what needs the children will have. The school has to pay the first £6,000 towards the one-to-one costs. It is not advised to budget for this eventuality and therefore any additional costs would show as an overspend in the budget. However, during the budget setting process the SENDCO is involved to ensure we have budgeted adequately for the current cohort.

Victoria
There are standard costs across both schools, therefore whilst the amount budgeted varies the budget accounts are very similar to Thomas Coram’s accounts.
BR explained that a whole school approach has been taken to increasing Nursery admission number, with the staff being advocates of the provision provided. There has been a very strong marketing campaign which has included flyers/postcards issued to local estate agents and residents.
Despite the reduction in birth rate the hard work and dedication by staff has resulted in 20 Nursery applications, with a further 4/5 applications in the pipeline
The budget includes 34 pupils for Reception; however, this has now increased to 36 pupils following the first round of continued interest. In future years BR advised that there were 31 Reception pupils budgeted each year, which would require two teachers. Therefore, the budget includes two Reception teachers, with a conservative income.
The Fund account will be used to update the staff room in 25/26, to support staff wellbeing.

Q -  How many children are in Nursery this year?
A – There were initially 17/18 at the beginning of the academic year, this has now risen to 25.

Q – Are there integrated contracts across the federation?
A - There are a number of contracts that both schools purchase such as those provided by HfL but all contracts remain separate. 

Q – There is an increase in staffing expenditure in 26/27, which then falls in future years, can you explain this figure?
A – This will be partly due to additional staffing being on one-year contracts, however, to provide a more in-depth response it was agreed that BR would review the budget and report back to governors.

BR advised that the budgets are looking very positive, as both schools balance over a 3-year period, which is not the general case across schools in Hertfordshire, with many struggling to balance in year 1. It has not been necessary to make any redundancies in this budget however some staff will be moving from Victoria to Thomas Coram due to excess staffing in Victoria: staff are employed by the Federation not the individual school.

Governors approved the budgets, governors thanked BR, LF, LH and LP for their hard work. MV left after the approval of the budget at 8pm, TB left at 7.50pm. | BR

5 | Risk Register review of Section 1 - Strategic and reputational risk

Governors agreed that when this document was originally created there were no highlighted concerns around pupil numbers, however it was agreed that the risk level should remain at moderate, due to the implemented mitigation. BR agreed to update the register with the additional mitigation.

Governors agreed that the risk concerning governors having the correct skills should move to moderate, based on the number of governor vacancies at the end of the summer term.

BJ queried that given Victoria’s Ofsted outcome, should the risk level be updated? Governors agreed that given the strong mitigation and the confidence that the objectives were being met and pupil numbers were increasing, the risk rating should remain the same.

It was agreed that LP and BR will review the risk register, including renumbering the document to make it more relevant and effective. The document will initially be sent to Tim for his review and then shared at the next Resources meeting. | BR and LP

The new DPO is Sharon Lindars.

4 | Review of spending some of the carry forward from TC
 
Solar panel review moved to the start of the meeting taken, prior to review of previous minutes and matters arising, to allow AB to leave following his presentation.

AB and TT have been carrying out a feasibility study (uploaded to Governor Hub) of installing solar panels at Thomas Coram School. AB advised an initial meeting was carried out with AT (site manager) following this, a report was commissioned which confirmed the roof was suitable for solar panel installation. Two proposals were made as part of the report, with proposal 1 recommended as the better design option by Sunsible LLP. AB advised the two options proposed were:

to install 75 solar panels on four roof areas, reducing the school’s electricity bill by approximately £6,307pa, producing 33% of the school’s electricity consumption, at a cost of £37,500. 
To install 41 panels across 2 roof areas, producing 21% of the school’s electricity consumption at a cost of £23,500

AB advised that the excess electricity generated would be exported to the grid and there would be no need for storage batteries on site, which can be unsightly and take up a lot of space.

Q – The proposal considers installing solar panels on the newer more modern building, will it supply both buildings? 
A- It would serve both buildings, with some additional wiring linking the electricity supply between the buildings. 

Q – In the second building the windows are of poor quality and the building lacks effective insulation, would it be cost-effective to spend money on solar panels?
A – Insulation would be the priority, to save energy by reducing heat loss and improve cost-effectiveness.

Q – Could you have a survey on the second building to review the windows as these are of poor quality?
A – The cost of replacing all the windows in the older building would be significant but could be considered as part of this review.

BR agreed that the replacement of the insulation and windows should be reviewed for the second building, however this may be cost prohibitive.

Governors approved that AB and TT could investigate funding options such as government and organisational grants and support from the diocese, to cover the upfront cost of installation

AB was thanked for his contribution and left the meeting at 7.35pm

Budget forecast review
BR and LP presented the most significant areas highlighted in the budget forecast (uploaded to governor hub).
 
Staffing
BR advised there had been a significant amount of sickness this academic year, which has had a significant impact on the budget. 

Q – Should the federation employ a member of staff to act as a cover staff member, on a permanent basis?
A – There are often two or three staff members absent across the various roles, which would make it difficult to employ one person. The cost of employing an agency worker permanently has been considered, however the buyout cost make this option less favourable, compared with using agencies to provide cover. A sickness insurance claim is also pending.

Q - Is sickness usually high?
A - It is often high and by using agency staff we are limiting the impact to that class, rather than spreading it across the school by using internal staff from other classes to cover.
LH advised that she is regularly covering one day a week to limit the impact on the budget, however this is challenging.

BJ agreed that backfilling creates additional challenges and that it makes sense not to pursue this route, however during the next budget year the federation may need to reconsider this and whether agency supply cover is financially sustainable.

Q - How much does it cost to employee an agency teacher?
A - £230.00 per day

Q – Are there any trends in sickness absence? 
A – There are no specific trends however, absence management has been reviewed in line with HCC trigger points, implementing performance plans where necessary. In addition to staff absence there has also been subject leadership time to cover which is essential to maintain, despite staff shortages.


Catering
LP advised governors that there has been a cost saving on UIFSM against the income received.

Q – How is the income and expenditure calculated for UIFSM?
A - The income is based on UIFSM actual numbers on the October and January census day, the expenditure is based on actual UIFSM numbers throughout the year, which can vary. The variances over the year can be either positive or negative, on the forecast a cost saving is shown for 24/25.

Water saving
LP advised there is a £7,000 credit with Castle Water due to incorrect billing, it will stay as a credit balance, with no further payments made until the credit balance is down to zero. BR advised there will be a 25% increase in water costs from 1st April, which is affecting all customers.

E19 – Learning resources
There is a £7000 underspend across learning resource budgets, which is due to the budget being set in April and the school priorities for the next academic year being reviewed in the summer term, after the approval of the budget. BR advised that this is true for all schools and BR prefers to overbudget than underbudget, to allow for contingencies.

TT informed governors that following a discussion with the science lead, the issue of a lack of science budget was raised, is this correct?
LH advised that this statement did not represent the budget allocated to science this year. Since April last year, there has been an increase in spending on science, including a £900 grant. Staff have also been advised that ‘wow days’ should also be included as part of their subject leadership, which would be allocated to their subject budget.

LF advised that Victoria have two whole school ‘wow day’ experiences per term, with ZooLab attending the school soon.

BR advised that all subject leaders are asked to collate a wish list as part of the budget setting process last year and the majority of requests were included in the 24/25 budget, however some of the underspend under E19 is due to the wish list items no longer being required by subject leaders.

IT overspend
LP advised there has been an increase in IT licences, including Pixl. In addition, the DfE advised LA’s that they now wanted to review the IT expenditure in schools in greater detail. This led to a number of new IT budget areas being created after the budget was set, which was beyond the control of schools but resulted in some areas of the budget being overspent and others being underspent. This has shown an increased expenditure under IT for 24/25. This has impacted all schools in Hertfordshire.

5 | SFVS

BR to consider how to progress and propose at next FGB.

 
Q - Does the Federation have a 3-year financial plan?
A – The Federation has a 5-year plan and this will be presented at the budget meeting in May as part of budget setting.

Benchmarking
The benchmarking data was shared with governors in advance of the meeting and BR presented the information, advising governors there were no surprises in the data which reinforced the SLT’s understanding of the key areas that impact the budget. BR highlighted the cost of staffing, which were higher than average, was largely down to significant investment in one to ones and interventions. BR also advised that governors could review cost per pupil, which can be benchmarked against other schools, highlighting that when pupil numbers decreased this figure would potentially increase as a class teacher is still required, regardless of whether the class is full.

BJ suggested that given the range of data available, a summary of information would be helpful. On review of the data during the meeting VH identified a report that provided a summary and uploaded these reports, for each school, to Governor Hub.

Bank Account review

Key areas identified by LP were:
Medical tracker was an unexpected cost but will be added to future budgets
£20,000 was spent from the Devolved Formula Capital (DFC) on toilets, in addition 10% must be contributed from the general account, which was included within the budget. LP advised that VAT cannot be claimed back on this expenditure.
Lettings – LP advised there is now an additional letting for netball resulting in increased income
LP informed governors that the phone upgrades will take place over half term 

Wi-Fi update at TC
BR advised governors that RH had allocated £5000 in the 23/24 budget to upgrade the Wi-Fi, which had not been completed and it was therefore carried forward to 24/25. BR has reviewed the options for Wi-Fi upgrades with Con-Ed, in line with the IT strategy. To provide a solution that would future proof the school for the next 10 years the cost would be approximately £7,300, which would be included in the 25/26 budget proposal. BR advised governors that the preference would be for Con-Ed to provide and install the equipment as they provide IT support to the school and have a clear understanding of the IT needs. BR has a second quote should the Wi-Fi equipment be purchased directly through NetGear (suppliers) rather than using Con-Ed. 

BR asked governors if they would be happy to approve the purchase through Con-Ed based on these two quotes, from the DFC in the 25/26 budget. Governors approved this request and BR agreed she would share the quotes with governors following the meeting.

Q – Is this a one-off cost?
A – Yes, there will be an annual licence cost of approximately £300.


TT advised there was a continued delay on the requested signature amendment through Natwest and whether a complaint could be raised. LP advised that there is a significant delay due to the large number of schools that have moved their Fund accounts to Natwest this financial year, with a large number of schools stating it has taken up to 12 months for accounts to be transferred. | BR

11 | Any other business

Ramp renovation
LF advised that ramp renovations between Nursery and Reception were planned for the Easter holidays, improving accessibility and outside space for children. This has required significant investment which has been raised through VSA fundraising and a £15,000 donation by Lawson Trust. LF advised this would consist of composite decking, due to minimal maintenance, and reinforced fencing. Two quotes have been obtained, one provided by an existing parent for £17,412 and a second quote for £24,114.

Lockdown procedures
BR provided an update on lockdown practices, clarifying the definition of ‘lockdown’ being if someone entered the site to cause damage or injury. A drill was conducted during the inset day to limit impact on children. BR advised that during the drill it was identified that staff could not hear the alarm in all areas therefore a walkie talkie system has been introduced for both schools. Teachers are already using walkie talkies and are therefore used to charging them each day, this procedure would ensure the majority of staff would be quickly alerted of an intruder. BR advised that an annual drill will take place on an inset day.

Ms R Roberts (BR, Exec Head)

1 | Welcome, Opening Prayers and Confidentiality Reminder
KH opened the meeting at 7pm and led the committee in prayer. Colleagues were reminded of the confidentiality of the meeting.

3 | Minutes of P&C meeting 2nd October.2024 and Matters Arising
The Governing Board approved the previous minutes, these will be marked as agreed on Governor Hub. No matters arising.

4 | Action points from meeting of 2nd October 2024:

BR to arrange for the subject leads to provide examples of the new Hertfordshire Writing Scheme at the next P&C meeting. (5)
BR to arrange for the Pixl presentation to be shared on Governor Hub - completed

5 | New writing curriculum update - LW
LW shared her presentation on Essentials Writing, which she will upload onto Governor Hub, following the meeting.
LW informed governors that the reason this scheme was chosen was research-based. One of the key elements that attracted the SLT to this scheme was the clear progression that can be identified for each child 
LW advised that this scheme encourages children to understand what they are going to write about and focuses on them writing as writers, considering the various steps including producing a draft, proof-reading, editing and presenting to a real audience.
LW stated that a strong aspect of the scheme is that the teaching of grammar is intrinsic and relevant.

The scheme also supports newer and experienced teachers with detailed unit plans supplied so teachers have a clear idea of how the lesson should be conducted, including adaptations for learners 

LW advised that the inclusion of explicit modelling within the scheme is the most effective way of teaching writing as it reviews how a writer writes and the impact on the reader. It also uses strong, high quality texts which are varied and support the children with the writing they are working on.

LW informed governors that the scheme had been used in Year 3 and 6 since October half term, as a soft launch, with this being rolled out to the whole school (Thomas Coram) from January. There has been a high level of positive feedback since the scheme was implemented. 

Victoria also introduced the scheme with Year 1 October half term, which had a powerful impact. LF advised that following book reviews and observations, she identified an improvement in the children’s understanding of the purpose of writing and has witnessed increased confidence in their abilities which has extended into other areas, such as spelling. LF informed governors that Victoria will now be trialling Reception.

Q – It looks very structured, and helpful and teacher feedback is really positive, is there an assessment element to the scheme?
A – The teachers assessment framework sits alongside the scheme, which are both produced by HfL. | LW

6 | Termly pupils' outcomes and monitoring

Assessment updates and impact of interventions and boosting

Thomas Coram
LH advised that assessments have taken place in September and January (this week and next), using Pixl. Children have not made as much progress as had been expected in writing, therefore the decision has been made to use Pixl for reading and maths whilst working with teachers to review the teacher assessments for writing. The English adviser is going to attend TC in March, to support this.

LH gave an example of the success of Pixl by advising that last year a Year 6 child was working at a Year 3 level and in Sept, when taking a SATS paper they were 5 marks away from achieving a age-related score. 

SG has been doing Maths papers in Year 4 and has seen a significant improvement, with some children who were achieving single figures out of 100, now achieving double figures. SG stated that Pixl supports the next steps, by using data analysis to identify the gaps and providing intervention lesson plans to help fill these gaps.
BR agreed that the interventions in Year 6 have been very effective and has also supported a smooth transition between a class teacher and a cover teacher (covering maternity leave).

LH advised that Year 6 will be doing their assessments this week, following the analysis of this data she will upload the information onto Governor Hub. 

Victoria
LF advised that Pixl has supported teacher assessment as some teachers are cautious when marking the children’s progress.

Baseline data has been conducted with Yr1, with reading writing and maths. Little Wandle has been an effective tool to monitor phonics in Reception and Year 1 and understanding specifically how a child is performing is very powerful. Those that are not highlighted as green, will be retaking their phonics. LF advised that there is clear evidence that Year 1 reading and fluency has becomes stronger through reteaching and consolidated learning. 

Q – A big priority is closing the gaps, as you have said, are you finding the schemes identify the gaps?
A – LH said she had not used Pixl before but one thing that appealed to her was managing the gaps and Pixl clearly identifies these gaps, following assessments. If there are whole class gaps, we have starter sessions during lessons and TA’s running interventions with small groups.

Q – How is Pixl embedding with staff, is it proving useful or a burden? 
A -  It is very useful and provides a consistent approach, it can pinpoint the gaps and provide the relevant resource to support teachers and TA’s to fill those gaps.

LF stated that Pixl is being used with Year 2, although they do not have the staffing to champion it in Victoria, due to the smaller pool of staff. LF agreed it is a very useful tool, however staff are struggling to find the time to use the resource as do not have an expert in school, so it will take more time to embed it. LH advised that Pixl is largely aimed at key stage 2 children, supporting children getting ready for their SATS.

BR informed governors that they have asked their Pixl expert to identify an infant school that are using Pixl effectively so they can arrange a visit to support expansion of the tool at Victoria.

Q- There has been a lot of time and effort when rolling out Pixl, will parents be informed?
A –The federation does not share the assessment processes, just the progress. In October parents evening parents were advised of their child’s gaps and this will continue in future parents’ evenings.

Governors agreed that the introduction of Pixl was already proving a success and looked forward to seeing further data in the future.

Pupil survey
BR advised that the pupil survey was conducted in November, prior to an SEA visit considering personal development. The areas highlighted in yellow, on the report, are areas that require further work, these were also areas that the children highlighted in their survey.

KH thanked Beccy for the information and agreed that the outcomes from the survey looked very good | LH

7 | PINS – update and action plan 

LH advised that she attended a meeting last week to review progress, working with a small team in Hertfordshire that work with staff individually and in classrooms, considering how lessons are structured and adaptive teaching. 

During learning walks LH and ST have seen adapted learning, which is a significant improvement. LH advised that they are expecting positive feedback from the PINS team when they visit next week.

8 | Intent, implementation, and impact of the curriculum update

BR advised that the current budget included HfL subject advisers reviewing the foundation subjects, considering how robust the plans are to ensure progression.  This has now taken place, reviewing all 4 areas (Art, D&T, Computing and Music) with two afternoon sessions per subject. The first meeting provided a review of current practices, the subject leader was then given the opportunity to consider this feedback before the second meeting, which agreed a way forward. This process required significant investment and based on the high level of positive feedback from teachers, it has been value for money. The main benefit being cited by staff is the consistent approach to progression from Year 2 to 6.
 
LF advised that staff appreciated the identification of key tasks that children should complete prior to moving to the next year group. 

Q –The joining up of the curriculum is one of the federations priorities, overall have teachers found this process useful?
A - Teachers have found this very useful. In addition, an inset day was spent looking at subject leadership, which provided the teachers with structured time to consider their subject and the expectations. The subject leaders of each school also worked together reviewing action plans, RAG ratings, priorities, strengths and time frames. The staff were given one month’s notice so they could prepare for the inset day, to ensure effective use of the day. The accountability of this exercise has been very beneficial and has provided BR and the Heads of both schools with a clear understanding of the next steps.

Q – Is this something staff are appraised on?
A – All teachers have a subject strategy, so they would be reviewed as part of the appraisal process.

BR advised that during the summer term there will be a governor’s curriculum report on each subject, collated into one document for each school.

NF stated that as the P&C meeting was in April, could it be moved to later in the term when the reports would be available, so they could be reviewed at the meeting. It was agreed that a change of dates would be considered by BR and EB outside of this meeting. | BR/EB

9 | SEA Visit feedback from 4th and 5th December – Personal Development deep dive

In addition, the marketing committee are also considering have a collection of testimonies on the website. LF and BR had been reviewing the SEF at Victoria and included some of these comments. Following a collective worship audit from the diocese, which was very productive, these quotes will also be valuable for the SIAMS. 

External monitoring – English, Maths and EYFS report
LF advised there have been a sequence of visits in EY, from the EY adviser, to review child initiating learning and looking at linking activities to themes and topics. Previously there was minimal thread and theme linked to activities, this process has now been simplified, with a working document now on the wall to ensure all adults understand the purpose of each activity. In addition, the planning had been very subject specific, now there is an overarching theme. These changes have had a positive impact on the team.

The next EY adviser visit will review the progression of those children that are struggling. 

Q – Are staff under a lot of pressure at the moment?
A – Staff absences at Victoria have been difficult and this increases the pressure on the team, however the EY visit was met with a positive approach and staff are now happier. Both teachers are relatively new to the role, these changes have reduced their workload and created more clarity over linking activities.

A – For the classroom the federation has invested in a programme called Storm breakers, this will build on movement breaks and mental wellbeing

BR advised that she has used it at her previous school which was very effective. Teachers have been building daily brain breaks into teaching but not consistently. Stormbreak, which is funded by Sports Premium, focusses on five different areas of mental wellbeing and resilience, providing a consistent approach across the whole federation which is enjoyable for children. BR agreed to provide an update on the progress at the next P&C meeting.

4 | Wellbeing Survey - TR to share action plan, following the Wellbeing Survey (from Resources on 14th May 2025)

31/80 staff responded (16 TC, 13 Victoria, 2 federation-wide) – governors queried the low level of responses, BR advised that given when the survey was carried out (last year), this was not surprising, however a recent communication survey has been carried out with a higher response rate.

The SENDCO at TC highlighted her high volume of direct parent contact. While necessary for certain matters, such as EHCP applications, parents will be reminded in the Autumn term that the class teacher should handle most queries first.

BR noted that some negative responses were provided by staff who do not undertake that particular role, rendering the answers irrelevant. Governors questioned whether such responses should be excluded from the data set; however, as no significant concerns were identified and the relevant roles could be identified, the data was retained.

BR recognised that staff absence at Victoria had a significant impact on morale, with staff covering additional duties and experiencing increased stress, Governors acknowledged that all possible steps had been taken to mitigate this.

Q – The feedback regarding safeguarding was surprising given that no significant safeguarding concerns have been reported recently

A – This was due to an increase in the use of CPOMS across various roles including Midday Supervisory Assistants, which has improved the information captured in CPOMS, but has given staff an additional task. Governors agreed this was a positive improvement.

Governors highlighted the negative comments regarding the use of display boards and felt that the boards added value. BR and LH agreed, explaining that although wall space is limited, the leadership team is committed to showcasing the importance of all subjects, and pupils take pride in displaying their work.

In conclusion BR advised Governors that whilst the data was useful, the information obtained through the communication survey has already proved more valuable, with some quick wins already identified. SLT will publish results of survey in October FGB. | CW agenda for FGB

5 | Governor roles:

EB advised Governors that following the recruitment of Chris Cartwright and potentially MT and TB moving from Associate Members to Governors, this will leave one vacancy, which will hopefully be filled next week.

EB thanked TT for volunteering to be Vice Chair of Governors, EB would mentor him to support his potential transition to Chair of Governors in September 2026, if he was successfully appointed.

The following governors also volunteered for specific roles:

MT – Vice Chair of Resources
MV – Chair of Admissions
N B-W – Chair of P&C, with the support from KH for the Autumn term as Co-Chair
TB and MV jointly taking on Complaints, G&A and Pupil & Staff discipline

EB asked Governors to review the roles document prior to the Strategy meeting, which would be updated in Governor Hub, and request any amendment necessary.

6 | 5 Year Strategic Plan

BR advised that the post it notes from the previous meeting were very useful and has identified the key points across the pillars:

Educational excellence linked to SIP in both schools including: reviewing key data points, consistency across internal monitoring and Year 4 multiplication check to improve outcomes.
Continuous improvement of the culture of safeguarding across the federation.
Happiness and Wellbeing including using Stormbreak in all classes to provide mental health and wellbeing physical breaks, staff and parent surveys, parent workshops and annual staff teambuilding event.
Community – highlighted as a key area where governors could support the federation with ideas to improve this area.
Sustainability – financial sustainability - review through SFVS audit at Victoria, supporting recruitment and retention, developing a digital strategy with support from Con-ed. Environmental sustainability – Developing a climate change action plan utilising online models 
Q – How is recruitment progressing in the federation?
A – Schools are continuing to find this a challenging area. Despite the Federation having links with universities and signing up to offer placements, it has been difficult, however, the teacher vacancy was successfully filled.

7 | Exec-Headteacher Report

Governors reviewed the reports and raised the following questions, with additional commentary provided by BR.

Payscales
BR advised governors that the SLT have been discussing pay structures, and there are people doing the same job across the federation but receiving different pay rates. While the financial impact isn’t significant, pay should be consistent and aligned across the board. Governors agreed this was a fair approach.

Q - What is the total cost?

A - £703 at Victoria and £1300 at TC in the first year, increasing in future years when staff move up their payscale.

Q – There has been some staff movement between TC and Victoria, has there been any significant budgetary impact?

A – As the movement filled a vacancy there has been no increase in costs at TC, but it has resulted in a reduction in costs at Victoria.

Carry forward
Q - Will there be any clawback based on the carry forward

A – The carry forward shall be allocated to larger projects, at which point the carry forward will be below the clawback threshold

SFVS audit

Q – Is any support required from Governors?

A – The audit is remote, and all the information requested has been submitted to the auditors. There will be a questionnaire for governors to complete in due course. 

BR thanked governors for their support and confirmed the audit would take place in September.

Nursery intake
Governors agreed the uptake in nursery applicants is excellent, with 26 confirmed applicants and a potential further two visiting the school next week.

Q - How do we know the upturn in figures has been based on the excellent work that has been carried out at Victoria? Are other schools securing a full cohort?

A - Many schools are struggling with admissions, with some nurseries closing. Victoria is in a very fortunate position; the hard work and dedication from the team has made a significant difference.

Vision and Values
Q – A year ago, we carried out a stakeholder consultation—how has the federation since developed its focus on vision and values with children and parents?

A – Children are now able to articulate the federation’s vision and values. Teachers and Heads of School are embedding them more actively in daily practice. At Victoria, roleplay activities and class discussions around vision and values have increased. The weekly newsletter now includes regular references to vision and values, and parents are engaging more, supported by initiatives such as the introduction of prayer bears (following the audit). The federation also maintains an active social media presence, showcasing how the vision and values are being demonstrated.

Governors agreed that there has been clear progress in embedding the vision and values across the federation.

Head of School’s Reports 

Victoria

Q – The report show “good” throughout, but there could be some areas described as “outstanding.” It doesn’t clearly highlight where we are excelling. 

A – The SEF identifies areas of strength as well as priorities for improvement and remains the key reference document. At Victoria, for example, attitudes and behaviour are judged to be outstanding.

Governors agreed how valuable some of the SEA visit quotes were and congratulated the school on graduating from the English Hub programme. 

Q - What personal development opportunities are there for SEND pupils in extracurricular activities? 

A - Attendance at clubs can be low for pupils with SEND, as they are often loud and noisy. A pupil voice exercise is planned to understand this further. Funding may be available through the Sports Premium or Pupil Premium if these pupils are considered disadvantaged. This aligns with our wider focus on supporting disadvantaged and vulnerable children, will now be referred as VIPs, very important pupils.

Q – Is the medical tracker used at Victoria?

A – Only TC use the tracker due to managing a higher number of pupils and less face to face contact with parents. The majority of injuries at Victoria are dealt with at the office and parents informed on collection. 

Q - Attendance monitoring – there has been a significant increase in unauthorised holidays. Is this seasonal, and how are we setting expectations with parents? Does the policy also apply to Nursery?

A: Attendance will be addressed at parents’ evening and discussed with teachers in September. Parents are required to apply for term-time leave, and attendance is being closely monitored. Confirmation will be sought regarding Nursery.


Q - The number of SEND parents has increased significantly, why is this?

A – Teachers are more rigorous in identifying children, with the SENDCO offering classroom support and engaging external services


Thomas Coram

Q - Can you explain what is meant by “fluid groupings”?	

A - In Years 4 and 5, pupils are organised into three groups, and in Year 6 there are four groups, some designed to provide additional support, others to extend learning.
A recent learning walk highlighted challenges within some groups, as a result, it was decided to introduce group splits in Years 5 and 6, but not in Year 4. This approach requires a fourth group to continue effectively. While the budget allows for three additional teachers, there are currently two (shared across Years 5 and 6), with additional TAs now supporting Years 3 and 4, which is proving effective.

Q: There are 103 SEND pupils—at what point would an additional SENDCO be needed?

A: The SENDCO provides support to teachers, who are handling the majority of the work. Her hours have increased to four days, but the emphasis is on the teachers implementing interventions in class., for example. She has also spent time at Swing Gate and Victoria to ensure effective handovers, both internally and with other schools.

Governors agreed the transition is very strong at Thomas Coram and Victoria.

Q: Regarding VIP pupils, how well are they accessing extracurricular clubs?

A: Only two children with an EHCP are currently attending clubs. Some do not wish to participate in sporting clubs, although a high number of SEN pupils do attend. LH has supported two children by accompanying them to clubs to help with their transition.

Attendance - LH advised governors that there is no significant attendance concerns overall, although there is an increase in unauthorised absence due to parents taking holidays in term time, often on a termly basis (10 weeks apart) therefore avoiding fines. There is also a high number of children experiencing emotional school avoidance. A new scheme is being trialled with one family to support attendance, given the significant amount of work only one family has been selected.

Governors noted the substantial work being undertaken.

8 | P2 monitoring reports 

Governors reviewed the P2 reports and raised the following questions:


Q – There is a shortfall of £7500 SEN funding, why is this?

A - This was entered into the budget across 3 terms, rather than 2..

Q – There are £1500 additional telephone charges, why is this?

A – The extended BT contract until July, along with some unbudgeted ongoing charges, caused this situation

Q: Why is there an increase in support staff costs (E03)?

A: The staff member was needed earlier than originally anticipated.

9 | BASH – mobile phones strategy – see Bridgewater documents on Gov Hub

BR advised Governors that at a recent BASH meeting the significant parental and school pressure around mobile phone use, particularly in secondary schools was raised.  If schools take a strong stance on this, it will support parents in setting boundaries. Ashlyns plans to introduce a mobile phone ban for Year 7 students from September 2026 and has asked schools to inform parents that, should they purchase a smartphone, this policy will apply at Ashlyns.

Q: From a parent’s perspective, it is much easier if there is a collective decision.
A: This is why SLT are supporting this approach. In secondary schools, mobile phones can cause behavioural issues. At Bridgewater, parents requested the ban of phones and the school have agreed for us to share this point with parents. The staff member leading the initiative is also willing to speak with our parents.

Governors confirmed they supported this decision. However, it was agreed that until Ashlyns decision has been ratified by their Governors BR will not share this information with parents. Discussions may develop within parent groups around the option of non-smartphones, but the school will not police this. It was also noted that some children rely on phones for practical purposes, such as paying for transport.

10 | Policies/Guidance for review include (on Gov Hub):

Code of Conduct - employees
Governors approved the Code of Conduct however some formatting issues on table of contents (point 15) required and a slight amendment to Beccy’s name to Ms Roberts for CW to complete prior to publishing.

13 | AOB

Safeguarding visit 

ID & VH reported the annual safeguarding audit shows no major concerns, CPOMS is well-used with spot-checks, and the single central record is fully up to date. VH advised that data is drawn from CPOMS to analyse what has been recorded across the school. The filtering and monitoring system and medical tracker is also reviewed, which Governors agreed are both being used effectively

An additional improvement has been enhancing the new-starter induction day which now incorporates all mandatory training.


Q - Can teachers access prevent training easily? There were some challenges when governors tried to locate the training
A – There is an online training course available for staff and Governors. It was agreed that ID would provide clarity for governors.






Private Therapists

BR advised that in both schools there are an increasing number of private therapists coming in to support children. Clubs pay a fee to use the premises, however the therapists are not charged. Our Lettings policy states all businesses will be charged. 

Q How many children are seen by private therapists?

A There are approximately 2-3 practioners, with 10-20 children being involved

Q – Does the school have an obligation to support this provision? If a charge is introduced will the therapist withdraw their service

A – There is no obligation. It can be beneficial for children, however there is the disadvantage that they are missing areas of the curriculum.

Governors agreed that LP will create a proposal to be reviewed in the next Resources meeting.

4 | Update of governor emergency contact details on Governor Hub
All governor contact details are up to date

5 | NB-W has agreed to take on roll of role of SEND/PPG link governor and will move to the P&C committee as this utilises her skill set. EB thanked SH for moving back to Resources, to allow this. EB will now focus on her new link role of Personal Development, Behaviour & Attitudes governor.

EB highlighted that BJ, KH and NF are stepping down and therefore including the current vacancy, there will be four foundation governor vacancies in September. The Diocese has provided some helpful guidance; however, the recruitment of governors must be in line with the Instrument of Governance. EB requested the support of governors to identify any potential candidates and direct them towards BR or EB.

Q – Would the number of foundation governors impact the outcome of a SIAMS visit?
A - Yes, the inclusion of foundation governors is of vital importance to the federation. The Instrument of Governance stipulates that there must be 9 Foundation Governors out of a total board of 16, in addition there must be a majority of 2 foundation governors over non-foundation governors.

Q - What obligation falls under the Diocese to appoint foundation governors?
A – Foundation governors must be practising Christians, and some are appointed by local churches. However local churches are struggling to recruit certain roles, such as church warden, within their own congregations, therefore filling a governor vacancy from the same pool, may prove challenging. 

Q - Could the federation contact churches outside the community?
A – This could be a possibility, if the vacancies cannot be filled. EB advised that she is meeting with SO next week, to discuss the matter.

MV suggested setting a timeframe for the initial approach through the local churches. If this proves unsuccessful, SO may be able to offer greater flexibility on suitable candidates. MV advised that he is happy to support the recruitment process. EB thanked MV for his offer of support and will discuss his suggestions with SO. | All governors
















EB

8 | HoS and Exec HT reports to governors
Progress towards the School Development Plan/ Federation action plan

Exec-Head’s report to governors

Governors thanked BR for her detailed Exec-Head report.

Q - Under vulnerable pupils there is reference to a federation plan, is there a timescale? 
A – BR informed governors that she met with a District SEA who leads on vulnerable pupils. The SEA shared a spreadsheet that calculates a vulnerability score based on the information that is populated about the child. Whilst BR is not considering allocating a score to pupils, it was a valuable exercise and highlighted that it is not just disadvantaged children that are vulnerable. The SEA will conduct staff training next term, promoting a culture change particularly around the type language used by staff and considering the impact of unconscious bias. During the meeting the SEA also highlighted the benefit of building relationships with parents, stating a supportive relationship can accelerate learning by 3 years.

BR advised that 37 Reception offers have been issued and therefore BR anticipates they will require two Reception classes in September. BR confirmed that if Reception numbers increase beyond 30, two teachers are required.

Q – If the school starts with 28 pupils and increases to 33, is another class required?
A – Yes, there are strict rules regarding Early Years ratios.

Thomas Coram HoS report
LH advised governors that the PINS training has been completed and a review is booked with the PINS team to consider the progress made. LH received a vast range of resources during the last PINS session, valuing approximately £400, these have been handed out to classes.

Victoria HoS report
LF advised that the moral within the school has improved significantly. The SEA visit included a lot of positive language and LF feels the school is now in a strong place and working through the Ofsted criteria. LF advised that the improvement over the past year has been fantastic and the reaffirmation from external sources is very motivational for the whole staffing team.
Progress towards SDP and Federation Action Plan

Q – What further support is required to move the whole school approach to resilience, to green? 
A – There have been other whole school focusses that have taken priority. However, during the summer term, 5 staff members will have 8 different training sessions. The information will be disseminated throughout the staffing team in September. 

Q - The SENCO roles and responsibilities area is in yellow; how are this being moved forward?
A – This area is ongoing, rather than not being met. Due to the nature of the role LH advised that there would always be ongoing changes to SENCO priorities.

16th June                  Admissions                            Online 
2nd July                    FGB Procedural                     TC

SEA visits: TC: 23/06/25
V: 26/06/25

Drop in Weeks: w/c 16th June – same writing focus

17 | Has the meeting been conducted in line with our vision and values? Has the board focused on all pupils and staff being able to flourish in learning and love? Has the meeting been conducted with kindness, respect, resilience, and thankfulness?

All governors agreed that it had been.

18 | Actions from meeting

CW to confirm, by 22/04/2025, if Safeguarding needs to be a standing item on every FGB agenda? 
All governors to actively support the recruitment of foundation governors, any potential candidates to be directed to EB/BR.
Prior to the FGB on 21st May, all governors to review the 5 Year strategic plan and advise EB/BR what area they would like to oversee.
Governors to provide staff with a one-week window to comment on their visit report, prior to uploading it to Governor Hub.
EB asked all governors to review ID’s report prior to the next governor visits, as the focus will be writing.
SG advised that she would review the governor visit forms prior to the next governor visit week (16th June) to support the inclusion of the vision and values being documented on the forms.
SH will chase SO (on his return from sabbatical) and NG to complete their safeguarding training. SH will forward details of the NGA members training to both governors.
Finance review to be added to the March FGB meeting each year.
Code of conduct was approved with a request for CW to add volunteers under point 1 above confidentiality.
