[SOURCE: FGB Minutes 2025-01-29.docx | Ofsted 26 Victoria /Minutes/FGB/2024-25 | Modified: 2025-09-28]

Kindness Respect Resilience Thankfulness 

Minutes of the Meeting of Governors held on 

Wednesday 29th January 2025 at 7pm at TC, 

Chaired by Elaine Bunn

Present:

There being no further business the meeting closed at 9pm. 

Ms R Roberts (BR, Exec Head)
Mrs E Bunn (EB, Chair)
Mrs S Giles (SG)
Mr T Trailor (TT)
Mrs K Hennessey (KH)
      Mrs T Brown (TB) | Mr M Thomson (MT)
Mr I Davies (ID)
Mrs S Holmes (SH)
Mrs N Few (NF)
Mrs N Boddam-Whetham (NBW)

Apologies received: Mrs L Hill (LH, Head of Thomas Coram), Fr S Owen (SO), Mrs B Jullien (BJ), 
Mr N Goss (NG), Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria), Mrs V Harris (VH)


Remote attendance: Mr M Vibert (MV)

Also in attendance: Simone Tyson (ST) | Apologies received: Mrs L Hill (LH, Head of Thomas Coram), Fr S Owen (SO), Mrs B Jullien (BJ), 
Mr N Goss (NG), Mrs L Freeman (LF, Head of Victoria), Mrs V Harris (VH)


Remote attendance: Mr M Vibert (MV)

Also in attendance: Simone Tyson (ST)

1 | Welcome, Opening Prayers and Confidentiality Reminder
EB opened the meeting at 7pm and led the FGB in prayer. Colleagues were reminded of the confidentiality of the meeting.

2 | Conflicts of Interest and Apologies for Absence
Apologies were received and accepted from LH, SO, BJ, NG, VH and LF
.
No conflicts of interest declared.

3 | Approval of Admissions Policy

EB asked Governors to approve the recommended decision by the Admissions Committee, on 13th January 2025, to approve the admissions policies and associated documents for Victoria and Thomas Coram for 2026-27. These policies were approved.

EB asked Governors to approve the proposed amendment to the Terms of Reference (ToR) for the Admissions Committee, allowing the Admissions Committee to approve all Admission policies and associated documents, without requiring FGB approval. There were some points that Governors approved this decision. (See Governing Hub for updated ToR).

KH raised a point that in the FGB ToR it states that the FGB meeting and associated minutes are open to the public. EB queried how the federation should manage remote meetings and how this should be made public, whether a link should be shared with the members of the public and how this should be communicated.

BR advised there has not been a demand for members of the public to attend the meetings in the past. ST advised that minutes are usually made available on a request basis, confirming that most schools do not upload minutes onto the website. KH queried why, at the beginning of meetings, are the governing body reminded of confidentiality if the minutes are open to the public. It was agreed that CW would investigate and feedback to governors.

KH referred to the P&C ToR Paragraph 9 bii) which stated that the committee should review the progress of more able pupils. KH felt that whilst the committee reviewed how the federation addressed closing the gaps on less able pupils, there was not clear evidence of reviewing those more able.

BR advised that she had attended a conference, which referred to the types of terminology used to describe the ability of children, as this can create divides. BR recommended that the ToR could be changed to refer to reviewing all pupils and the progress of all groups of children, which would include specific educational needs, disadvantaged pupils and any other targeted groups that are being monitored. KH agreed that the terminology is important but also what actions are needed by governors. It was agreed that this would be put on the agenda for the next P&C meeting, 

Governors advised that the numbering on the ToR’s requires some adjustment - CW to update document and re-upload to Governor Hub.

EB advised that under the ToR for the Admission Committee it referred to Governors, however as NG is the chair and is an Associate Member this term was replaced with Governor members to enable NG to remain as chair and to be included within the required quorate of 3. (Following the meeting CW advised that NG cannot be included within the quorate, as Associate Members are not included for quorate calculations). | CW












CW



CW

4 | Appointment of NBW to Governing Body
EB formally confirmed the appointment of Nicci Boddam-Whetham to the Castle Federation as a PCC Governor, who will be part of the Resources Committee. Governors approved Nicci’s appointment.

5 | Training sessions on Effective Governance

ST was thanked for her valuable training course.

The transcript and training session video will be shared with those Governors who were unable to attend the meeting. | CW

6 | Meeting dates 2024-25

14th May 	-	Resources			Online

2nd July	-	FGB Procedural		TC 

SEA visits: TC: 25/03/25, 23/06/25
                     V: 05/02/2025, 19/03/25, 26/06/25

Drop in Weeks: w/c 3rd March, w/c 16th June

7 | Has the meeting been conducted in line with our vision and values? Has the board focused on all pupils and staff being able to flourish in learning and love? Has the meeting been conducted with kindness, respect, resilience, and thankfulness?

All governors agreed that it had been.

8 | Actions from meeting

CW to add review of P&C ToR section 9 bii) to the next P&C meeting, to determine monitoring of all groups of children.
CW to investigate the confidentiality of meetings/minutes if a member of the public wants to attend an FGB meeting or review the minutes.
CW to correct numbering on ToR.
CW to upload recording of meeting to Governor Hub.

Church of England Vision for
Education: ‘Life in all its fullness’
Lizzie Jeanes and Ryan Parker
Diocese of St Albans

Leadership Pedagogy Theology
Vision for Education
Life in all its fullness

Educating for
Educating for
Wisdom, Knowledge
Hope and Aspiration
and Skills
‘Life in all
its fullness’
Educating for
Educating for Dignity
Community and
and Respect
Living Well Together

its full | ness’

Educating for Wisdom,
Knowledge and Skills:
Fostering discipline, confidence and
delight in seeking wisdom and knowledge,
and fully developing talents in all areas of
life.

Educating for Hope and
Aspiration:
Seeking healing, repair and renewal,
coping wisely with things and people
going wrong, opening horizons and
guiding people into ways of fulfilling them.

Educating for Community and
Living Well Together:
Ensuring a core focus on relationships,
participation in communities and the
qualities of character that enable people to
flourish together.

Educating for
Dignity and Respect:
Ensuring the basic principle of respect for
the value and preciousness of each person,
treating each person as a unique individual
of inherent worth.

How effective is the school’s distinctive Christian vision,
established and promoted by leadership at all levels,
in enabling pupils and adults to flourish?
Vision, linked to context, and shared with community.
What do you do because of your Christian vision?
(Actions taken, decisions made)
How do you know it is working? (Impact)

Requires schools to have a theologically rooted
Christian vision that is sensitive to and significantly
shaped by the school’s context.
onte
x
C
t
Theologically rooted
Christian vision

A theologically-rooted Christian vision is one that finds its roots, its starting
place, in biblical and Christian teaching. Such a vision draws on the life and
teaching of Christ, and wider aspects of the bible and Christian thought, to
influence the ‘why’, ‘what’ and ‘how’ of school life in a way which
resonates/connects deeply with the needs of the community.

a) How is the school’s vision a clearly-articulated, theologically rooted Christian vision?
How does the trust’s vision resonate with this?
b) How do the specific needs of the school community inform the theologically rooted
Christian vision? In other words, do leaders understand the school’s context, and do
they know how to respond to it theologically?
c) Why have school leaders decided that the school should be a maintained school/an
academy? How does this status enhance the effectiveness of the school as a Church
Take time now to consider the following school?
questions in your workbook, particularly d) As a result of the school’s Christian vision, original foundation, and current context, why
are school and trust structures of governance as they are?
a and b.
e) How do governance accountability and delegated authority in the school and trust
enhance the work of the school as a Church school? How do leaders know this?
We will both be around should you want
g) What are the school’s arrangements for collective worship? Why are these
to discuss one-to-one.
arrangements in place?
h) How is religious education structured and organised? Why have these decisions been
made?
i) What is the relationship between the school/trust and the DBE and/or MAST? How do
these relationships enhance the school’s ability to live out its Christian vision and to live
up to its foundation as a Church school, enabling people to flourish?
j) What is the relationship between the school/trust and local church/es? How do these
relationships enhance the school’s ability to live out its Christian vision and to live up to
its foundation as a Church school, enabling people to flourish?

How is the school’s vision a clearly-articulated, theologically rooted Christian vision?

What questions do you have here?

Context → Vision → Provision → Flourishing

Explored through seven areas/inspection questions:
IQ 1 - How does the school’s theologically rooted Christian vision enable pupils and adults to flourish?
IQ 2 - How does the curriculum reflect the theologically rooted Christian vision?
IQ 3 - How is daily collective worship enabling pupils and adults to flourish spiritually?
IQ 4 - How does the school’s theologically rooted Christian vision create a culture in which pupils and adults
are treated well?
IQ 5 - How does the school’s theologically rooted Christian vision create an active culture of justice and
responsibility?
IQ 6 - Is the religious education curriculum effective (with reference to the expectations set out in the
Church of England’s Statement of Entitlement for Religious Education)?
VA Schools - IQ 7 - What is the quality of religious education in voluntary aided and former voluntary aided
schools, and in former voluntary controlled schools in which denominational religious education is taught?

IQ2 - How does the curriculum reflect the theologically rooted Christian vision?
a) In what ways does the theologically rooted Christian vision shape the curriculum, including the extra-
curricular offer?
b) How is spiritual development an intrinsic part of the curriculum?
c) How do leaders know that the curriculum is having the intended effect for pupils?
d) How, specifically, does the Christian vision shape the learning experience for pupils who are deemed
to be vulnerable and/or disadvantaged?
e) How does being part of the trust enhance the school’s curriculum?

IQ2 - How does the curriculum reflect the theologically rooted Christian vision?
a) In what ways does the theologically rooted Christian vision shape the curriculum, including the extra-curricular offer?
b) How is spiritual development an intrinsic part of the curriculum?
c) How do leaders know that the curriculum is having the intended effect for pupils?
d) How, specifically, does the Christian vision shape the learning experience for pupils who are deemed to be vulnerable and/or
disadvantaged?
e) How does being part of the trust enhance the school’s curriculum?
o What is your curriculum and why have you developed it?
o How do staff understand the impact of the vision on the curriculum?
o How do you know/how can you help them to know?

IQ3 - How is collective worship enabling pupils and adults to flourish spiritually?
a) How do the theologically rooted Christian vision and the Anglican foundation of the school shape worship and spirituality in the
school?
b) How do partnerships with the DBE and partnerships with parish/local church/es enhance this?
c) In what ways is the worship life of the school inclusive, invitational, and inspirational?
d) In the context of the school as a Church school, what do pupils and adults understand to be the meaning of spirituality and
spiritual development? How does this enhance and enrich collective worship and individuals’ spiritual development?
e) How does the trust contribute to and enhance the school’s worship and spiritual life?
o How does your school understand ‘spiritual flourishing’? What does the school think
this looks like?
o How is this enabled/enhanced through worship?
o What is the impact of collective worship upon pupils and adults spiritual flourishing?

Summary
• There will be a firm expectation of a theologically rooted Christian
vision.
• There will be an enhanced freedom to be a Christian-vision-driven
Church school in the specific context of the school.
• Freedom also from an exhaustive one-size fits all set of criteria.
• Attention on the role of trust leaders in helping church schools flourish
